 September 26, 2024 U.S. General Services Administration The Heartland Region, Region 6 2300 Main Street Kansas City, MO 64108 Subject: GSA eOffer Submission Reference: GSA Solicitation 47QSMD20R0001: Multiple Award Schedule (MAS) Dear GSA, On behalf of National Security Innovations, Inc. (NSI), we express our appreciation for the opportunity to present our qualifications to the General Services Administration (GSA) in response to subject solicitation. NSI is a professional services firm specializing in multidisciplinary data -driven analytics. Our niche is helping clients better and more reliably understand people and their behaviors on critical, complex decision -making problems. Our highly diverse and experienced team of researchers and analy sts apply multidisciplinary social science techniques and various analytic methods to create deeper analyses and clarifying insights enabling our clients to make more informed and better decisions. Over the last decade, NSI has worked on hundreds of projects for government and commercial clients. Our clients have become increasingly aware of the importance of accounting for the human component in their analytical and decision -making processes. NSI represents that all data submitted in response to the Solicitation No. 47QSMD20R0001, including all additional information provided to the Government is current, accurate, and complete. NSI attests that there have been no exceptions taken to other term s and conditions of this solicitation and agrees to comply with the requirements of all clauses and provisions. NSI understands and has read the entire MAS solicitation and is confident that the following documentation was developed within all Terms & Conditions as defined in SCP -FSS-001. We certify that no changes have been made to solicitation 47QSMD20R0001 and electronic copies submitted are identical to the Request for Proposal provided in conjunction with the above solicitation. Should the reviewing Contracting Officer have any questions on any part of the offer, NSI requests that we will have the opportunity to answer any clarifications or deficiencies prior to rejection. Internally, NSI has marked the GSA process as a high -prior ity and has staff dedicated and ready to respond to GSA clarifications and negotiations in an expedited manner. Coley GCS, LLC, as a consultant to NSI has assisted and advised us in the preparation and submission of this offer and will be our primary point of contact and authorized negotiators throughout GSA’s review. We have enclosed the Agent Authorization Letter and state here as well that we authorize Coley GCS, LLC to act on our behalf for administrative functions, provide and submit clarification changes, and assist in the negotiation of our GSA contract award prices, terms, and conditions. Please notify Ramiro R Delgado, an authorized negotiator, when a contracting officer is assigned to review the offer. Should GSA have any questions or require further information, please contact Mr. Delgado at (210) 402-6766 or by email at rdelgado@coleygcs.com . Respectfully Submitted, National Security Innovations, Inc. ___________________________ Bryan Rasmussen VP of Operations

DISCLOSURE OF OWNERSHIP OR CONTROL BY THE GOVERNMENT OF A COUNTRY THAT IS A STATE SPONSOR OF TERRORISM (SEP 2021) (a) Definitions. As used in this provision- "Government of a country that is a state sponsor of terrorism" includes the state and the government of a country that is a state sponsor of terrorism, as well as any political subdivision, agency, or instrumentality thereof."Significant interest" means- (1) Ownership of or beneficial interest in 5 percent or more of the firm's or subsidiary's securities. Beneficial interest includes holding 5 percent or more of any class of the firm's securities in "nominee shares," "street names," or some other method of holding securities that does not disclose the beneficial owner; (2) Holding a management position in the firm, such as a director or officer; (3) Ability to control or influence the election, DFARS 252.225-7050 Sep 2021 DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 9 of 81 appointment, or tenure of directors or officers in the firm; (4) Ownership of 10 percent or more of the assets of a firm such as equipment, buildings, real estate, or other tangible assets of the firm; or (5) Holding 50 percent or more of the indebtedness of a firm. "State sponsor of terrorism" means a country determined by the Secretary of State, under section 1754(c)(1)(A (i) of the Export Control Reform Act of 2018 (Title XVII, Subtitle B, of the National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2019, Pub. L. 115-232), to be a country the government of which has repeatedly provided support for acts of international terrorism. As of the date of this provision, state sponsors of terrorism include: Iran, North Korea, Sudan, and Syria. (b) Prohibition on award. In accordance with 10 U.S.C. 2327, unless a waiver is granted by the Secretary of Defense, no contract may be awarded to a firm if the government of a country that is a state sponsor of terrorism owns or controls a significant interest in- (1) The firm; (2) A subsidiary of the firm; or (3) Any other firm that owns or controls the firm. (c) Representation. Unless the Offeror submits with its offer the disclosure required in paragraph (d) of this provision, the Offeror represents, by submission of its offer, that the government of a country that is a state sponsor of terrorism does not own or control a significant interest in- (1) The Offeror; (2) A subsidiary of the Offeror; or (3) Any other firm that owns or controls the Offeror. (d) Disclosure. (1) The Offeror shall disclose in an attachment to its offer if the government of a country that is a state sponsor of terrorism owns or controls a significant interest in the Offeror; a subsidiary of the Offeror; or any other firm that owns or controls the Offeror. (2) The disclosure shall include- (i) Identification of each government holding a significant interest; and DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 10 of 81 (ii) A description of the significant interest held by each government. (D)  HAVE NOT , within a three-year period FAR 52.209-5 Aug 2020 DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 17 of 81 preceding this offer, been notified of any delinquent Federal Taxes in an amount that exceeds the threshold at 9.104-5(a)(2) for which the liability remains unsatisfied. (1) Federal taxes are considered delinquent if both of the following criteria apply: (i) The tax liability is finally determined. The liability is finally determined if it has been assessed. A liability is not finally determined if there is a pending administrative or judicial challenge. In the case of a judicial challenge to the liability, the liability is not finally determined until all judicial appeal rights have been exhausted. (ii) The taxpayer is delinquent in making payment. A taxpayer is delinquent if the taxpayer has failed to pay the tax liability when full payment was due and required. A taxpayer is not delinquent in cases where enforced collection action is precluded. (2) Examples: (i) The taxpayer has received a statutory notice of deficiency, under I.R.C.6212, which entitles the taxpayer to seek Tax Court review of a proposed tax deficiency. This is not a delinquent tax because it is not a final tax liability. Should the taxpayer seek Tax Court review, this will not be a final tax liability until the taxpayer has exercised all judicial appeal rights. (ii) The IRS has filed a notice of Federal tax lien with respect to an assessed tax liability, and the taxpayer has been issued a notice under I.R.C. 6320 entitling the taxpayer to request a hearing with the IRS Office of Appeals contesting the lien filing, and to further appeal DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 18 of 81 to the Tax Court if the IRS determines to sustain the lien filing. In the course of the hearing, the taxpayer is entitled to contest the underlying tax liability because the taxpayer has had no prior opportunity to contest the liability. This is not a delinquent tax because it is not a final tax liability. Should the taxpayer seek tax court review, this will not be a final tax liability until the taxpayer has exercised all judicial appeal rights. (iii) The taxpayer has entered into an installment agreement pursuant to I.R.C.6159. The taxpayer is making timely payments and is in full compliance with the agreement terms. The taxpayer is not delinquent because the taxpayer is not currently required to make full payment. (iv) The taxpayer has filed for bankruptcy protection. The taxpayer is not delinquent because enforced collection action is stayed under 11 U.S.C 362 (the Bankruptcy Code). (ii) The Offeror ,  HAS NOT , within a three-year period preceding this offer, had one or more contracts terminated for default by any Federal agency. The offeror certifies, to the best of its knowledge and belief, that the offeror and/or any of its principals- (1)  ARE NOT presently debarred, suspended, proposed for debarment, or declared ineligible for the award of contracts by any Federal agency; (2)  HAVE NOT , within a three-year period preceding this offer, been convicted of or had a civil judgment rendered against them for: commission of fraud or a criminal offense in connection with obtaining, attempting to obtain, or performing a Federal, state or local government contract or subcontract; violation of Federal or state antitrust statutes relating to the submission of offers; or commission of embezzlement, theft, forgery, bribery, falsification or destruction of records, making false statements, tax evasion, violating Federal criminal tax laws,or receiving stolen property; (3)  ARE NOT presently indicted for, or otherwise criminally or civilly charged by a Government entity with, commission of any of these offenses enumerated in paragraph (h)(2) of this clause; and (4)  HAVE NOT within a three-year period preceding this offer, been notified of any delinquent Federal taxes in an amount that exceeds the threshold at 9.104-5(a)(2) for which the liability remains unsatisfied. (i) Taxes are considered delinquent if both of the following criteria apply: (A) The tax liability is finally determined. The liability is finally determined if it has been assessed. A liability is not finally determined if there is a pending administrative or judicial challenge. In the case of a judicial challenge to the liability, the liability is not finally determined until all judicial appeal rights have been exhausted. (B) The taxpayer is delinquent in making payment. A taxpayer is delinquent if the taxpayer has failed to pay the tax liability when full payment was due and required. A taxpayer is not delinquent in cases where enforced collection action is precluded. (ii) Examples: (A) The taxpayer has received a statutory notice of deficiency, under I.R.C.6212, which entitles the taxpayer to seek Tax Court review of a proposed tax deficiency. This is not a delinquent tax because it is DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 36 of 81 not a final tax liability. Should the taxpayer seek Tax Court Review, this will not be a final tax liability under the taxpayer has exercised all judicial appeal rights. (B) The IRS has filed a notice of Federal tax lien with respect to an assessed tax liability, and the taxpayer has been issued a notice under I.R.C.6320 entitling the taxpayer to request a hearing with the IRS Office of Appeals contesting the lien filing, and to further appeal to the Tax Court if the IRS determines to sustain the lien filing. In the course of the hearing, the taxpayer is entitled to contest the underlying tax liability because the taxpayer has had no prior opportunity to contest the liability. This is not a delinquent tax because it is not a final tax liability. Should the taxpayer seek tax court review, this will not be a final tax liability until the tax payer has exercised all judicial appeal rights. (C) The taxpayer has entered into an installment agreement pursuant to I.R.C.6159. The taxpayer is making timely payments and is in full compliance with the agreement terms. The taxpayer is not delinquent because the taxpayer is not currently required to make full payment. (D) The taxpayer has filed for bankruptcy protection. The taxpayer is not delinquent because enforced collection action is stayed under II U. S. C 362 (the Bankruptcy Code). A "Y" indicates "Small" and "N" indicates "Other than Small." This status is derived from the SBA's size standards based on the size metrics you entered. (a) Definitions. As used in this provision- "Economically disadvantaged women owned small business (EDWOSB) concern" means a small business concern that is at least 51 percent directly and unconditionally owned by, and the management and daily business operations of which are controlled by, one or more women who are citizens of the United States and who are economically disadvantaged in accordance with 13 CFR part 127, and the concern is certified by SBA or an approved third-party certifier in accordance with 13 CFR 127.300. It automatically qualifies as a women-owned small business concern eligible under the WOSB Program. "Service-disabled veteran-owned small business concern" (1) Means a small business concern- (i) Not less than 51 percent of which is owned by one or more service-disabled veterans or, in the case of any publicly owned business, not less than 51 percent of the stock of which is owned by one or more service-disabled veterans; and (ii) The management and daily business operations of which are controlled by one or more service- disabled veterans or, in the case of a service- disabled veteran with permanent and severe disability, the spouse or permanent caregiver of such veteran. (2) "Service-disabled veteran" means a veteran, as defined in 38 U.S.C. 101(2), with a disability that is service-FAR 52.219-1 MAR 2023 DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 48 of 81 connected, as defined in 38 U.S.C. 101(16). "Small business concern" (1) Means a concern, including its affiliates, that is independently owned and operated, not dominant in its field of operation, and qualified as a small business under the criteria in 13 CFR part 121 and the size standard in paragraph (b) of this provision. (2) Affiliates as used in this definition, means business concerns, one of whom directly or indirectly controls or has the power to control the others, or a third party or parties control or have the power to control the others. In determining whether affiliation exists, consideration is given to all appropriate factors including common ownership, common management, and contractual relationships. SBA determines affiliation based on the factors set forth at 13 CFR 121.103. "Small disadvantaged business concern," consistent with 13 CFR 124.1002, means a small business concern under the size standard applicable to the acquisition, that (1) Is at least 51 percent unconditionally and directly owned (as defined at 13 CFR 124.105) by- (i) One or more socially disadvantaged (as defined at 13 CFR 124.103) and economically disadvantaged (as defined at 13 CFR 124.104) individuals who are citizens of the United States, and (ii) Each individual claiming economic disadvantage has a net worth not exceeding $750,000 after taking into account the applicable exclusions set forth at 13 CFR 124.104(c)(2); and (2) The management and daily business operations of which are controlled (as defined at 13 CFR 124.106) by individuals who meet the criteria in paragraphs (1)(i) and (ii) of this definition. "Veteran-owned small business concern" means a small business concern- (1) Not less than 51 percent of which is owned by one or more veterans (as defined at 38 U.S.C. 101(2)) or, in the case of any publicly owned business, not less than 51 percent of the stock of which is owned by one or more veterans; and (2) The management and daily business operations of which are controlled by one or more veterans. "Women-owned small business concern" means a small business concern- DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 49 of 81 (1) That is at least 51 percent owned by one or more women; or, in the case of any publicly owned business, at least 51 percent of the stock of which is owned by one or more women; and (2) Whose management and daily business operations are controlled by one or more women. "Women-owned small business (WOSB) concern eligible under the WOSB Program" (in accordance with 13 CFR part 127) means a small business concern that is at least 51 percent directly and unconditionally owned by, and the management and daily business operations of which are controlled by, one or more women who are citizens of the United States, and the concern is certified by SBA or an approved third-party certifier in accordance with 13 CFR 127.300. As used in this provision- (1) "Effectively owned or controlled" means that a foreign government or any entity controlled by a foreign government has the power, either directly or indirectly, whether exercised or exercisable, to control the election, appointment, or tenure of the Offeror's officers or a majority of the Offeror's board of directors by any means, e.g., ownership, contract, or operation of law (or equivalent power for unincorporated organizations). (2) "Entity controlled by a foreign government"- (i) Means- (A) Any domestic or foreign organization or corporation that is effectively owned or controlled by a foreign government; or (B) Any individual acting on behalf of a foreign government. (ii) Does not include an organization or corporation that is owned, but is not controlled, either directly or indirectly, by a foreign government if the ownership of that organization or corporation by that foreign government was effective before October 23, 1992. (3) "Foreign government" includes the state and the government of any country (other than the United States and DFARS 252.209-7002 JUN 2010 DOWNLOADED ON Apr 12, 2024 AT 02:00:02 PM GMT Page 67 of 81 its outlying areas) as well as any political subdivision, agency, or instrumentality thereof. (4) "Proscribed information" means- (i) Top Secret information; (ii) Communications security (COMSEC) material, excluding controlled cryptographic items when unkeyed or utilized with unclassified keys; (iii) Restricted Data as defined in the U.S. Atomic Energy Act of 1954, as amended; (iv) Special Access Program (SAP) information; or (v) Sensitive Compartmented Information (SCI). (b) Prohibition on award. No contract under a national security program may be awarded to an entity controlled by a foreign government if that entity requires access to proscribed information to perform the contract, unless the Secretary of Defense or a designee has waived application of 10 U.S.C. 2536(a). (c) Disclosure. The Offeror shall disclose any interest a foreign government has in the Offeror when that interest constitutes control by a foreign government as defined in this provision. If the Offeror is a subsidiary, it shall also disclose any reportable interest a foreign government has in any entity that owns or controls the subsidiary, including reportable interest concerning the Offeror's immediate parent, intermediate parents, and the ultimate parent. Factor One: Corporate Experience Use or disclosure of data contained on this sheet is subject to the restriction on the title page of this proposal. National Security Innovations, Inc. Proprietary Information THE NUMBER OF YEARS OF CORPORATE EXPERIENCE IN PROVIDING THE PRODUCTS /SERVICES DESCRIBED UNDER THIS SCHEDULE National Security Innovations, Inc., ( NSI), is a certified Veteran Owned Small Business (VOSB) founded in 2007 headquartered in Boston, Massachusetts. Our focus has been to deliver innovative social science solutions to government client s for a variety of national security and operational imperatives. Our government clients want insights and a rich understanding of the overwhelming complexity of people and their behaviors for various critically important and complex decision-making problems. In 2011, expanding and diversifying our client base was a top priority. Our strategy was to provide analytical ex pertise to clients in the commercial sector needing to better understand customers and their behaviors. We focused on bringing greater discipline to measuring customer interactions, sentiment, and service. We successfully piloted a project with a major video game developer then and since has substantially grown this work. ORGANIZATION 'S NUMBER OF EMPLOYEES , EXPERIENCE IN THE FIELD , AND RESOURCES AVAILABLE TO ENABLE IT TO FULFILL REQUIREMENTS No. of Employees: NSI is comprised of 20 employees. Mission Statement: Create value for our clients by improving their decision-making processes by questioning assumptions, thinking deeply, and generating clarifying insights. Vision Statement: Enable clients to make more informed and better decisions on complex decision- making problems through our multidisciplinary data -driven analytics. Resources: At NSI, our greatest asset is our people. Our unique, unified company culture attracts brilliant, creative, well-credentialed professionals who share an entrepreneurial spirit and ardent desire to make a true difference for customers. Our commitment to taking care of our people inspires the dedication and longevity of our teams, ensuring success and continuity for client initiatives. B RIEF HISTORY OF THE OFFEROR 'S ACTIVITIES CONTRIBUTING TO THE DEVELOPMENT OF EXPERTISE AND CAPABILITIES RELATED TO THIS REQUIREMENT . NSI has been a leader in strengthening our nation's security by providing innovative and pragmatic scientific, technical, analytical, and programmatic services, research products, and technologies to complex 21 st century national security problems. NSI's unique approach to national security is to couple and leverage quantitative/computational modeling and analytical methods with principles from the social, physical, and information sciences. NSI has a very unique multi-disciplinary staff that includes natio nally recognized leaders and pioneers in socio -cultural matters, national security matters, former tenured professors, and individuals with broad operational and domain expertise including in-country deployments to Iraq and Afghanistan. Our customers and partners include the US Government, defense industry, intelligence community, FFRDCs, national labs, and academic institutions. INFORMATION THAT DEMONSTRATES THE OFFEROR 'S ORGANIZATIONAL AND ACCOUNTING CONTROLS . Organization : As noted in our Organization Chart, a key aspect to NSI’s overall approach to successfully executing the scope of work is to provide open and direct lines of communication to support effective collaboration. Accounting : NSI utilizes QuickBooks accounting software which ensures our compliance with generally accepted accounting principles and allows cost accounting by each specific customer. QuickBooks will enable us to easily identify GSA Schedule contract awards and accurately report quarterly sales to GSA. A DESCRIPTION OF THE RESOURCES PRESENTLY IN -HOUSE OR THE ABILITY TO ACQUIRE THE TYPE AND KINDS OF PERSONNEL /PRODUCTS PROPOSED . Factor One: Corporate Experience Use or disclosure of data contained on this sheet is subject to the restriction on the title page of this proposal. National Security Innovations, Inc. Proprietary Information At NSI, our professional services firm specializing in multidisciplinary data -driven analytics. Our researchers and analysts have expertise in social psychology, statistics, research methods, economics, cultural anthropology, decision science, business management, predictive modeling, political science, international relations, communications, mathematics, computer science, and other disciplines. NSI has significant expertise and many years of hands -on experience applying quantitative, qualitative, and mixed -method research and analytic methods. NSI’s leadership is comprised of nationally recognized experts with diverse backgrounds from premier government, industry, and academic institutions. They include current and former professors from top universities, former senior Defense Department and ind ustry executives, and members/co -chairs of National Academy of Sciences studies. Recruitment : Our in -house professional recruiting staff members work in step with our program management team to effectively utilize the plan, which offers fully integrated social media platforms, target niche job boards, electronic onboarding, and complete requisition and offer management. NSI’s recruitment professionals ensure that the selection, screening, clearance verification, and hiring processes for this work are efficient, consistent, and effective at each step. Once candidates are identified, our recruitment staff efficiently match personnel against work requirements— expediting identification of the most highly qualified, experienced, and available candidates. A DESCRIPTION OF THE MARKETING STRATEGY THAT WILL BE USED TO REACH FEDERAL ORDERING ACTIVITIES . Over the last decade, NSI has supported many government and commercial clients from defense, intelligence, gaming, digital entertainment, business intelligence, and customer service. We have provided solutions to a wide variety of critical analytical and d ecision -making problems. Our solutions have enabled our clients to better understand people and their behaviors such as at -risk populations, market segments, multiplayer engagement, brand loyalty, and customer satisfaction . We believe that these organizati ons will benefit the most from our services as they often require more advanced solutions to maintain their competitive edge. We understand the US Government is the number one buyer of goods and services in the world, and offering services awarded under our own GSA Schedule contract is simply our first step in marketing to the US Government. At NSI we plan on taking steps to publicize our MAS GSA Schedule. We also understand by uploading our awarded GSA Pricelist on GSA eLibrary, Federal agencies will have open access to our GSA awarded services catalog. In addition, we intend to utilize GSA’s eBuy system to the fullest extent pos sible and will have federal sales professionals on our government services branch fully dedicated to responding to Request for Quote (RFQs) and Request for Proposal (RFPs). Projected sales: NSI anticipates sales of at least $ 125,000 annually during our first full contract year on the GSA Schedule. We believe these sales will come through the diversion of existing Federal Government sales, reselling software with niche technology capabilities, as well as identifying and cultivating new clients. A DISCUSSION REGARDING THE INTENDED USE OF SUBCONTRACTORS . As a small business, NSI is not required to use subcontractors in the delivery of our services. However, if the need arises, we will use subcontractors to deliver full solutions to our customers. NSI is able to propose a variety of positions as our comprehensive recruitment and screening program allows us to select high -level talent with appropriate certifications and qualifications. NSI recruits and fields the talent required to transform, sustain, and secure enterprise federal environments.

Our approach is to baseline existing Quality Control (QC) processes and to validate current metrics and objectives. From this baseline, we will work with the project and TO stakeholder to determine if documented processes and measures are effective and determine if additional ones may be required to meet quality standards. The QC process will help our Program Manager (PM) to monitor and control project services – by identifying and correcting deficiencies in quality performance before they become unacceptable – and to assist in continuous improvement of service. IDENTIFICATION OF INDIVIDUALS RESPONSIBLE FOR ENSURING QUALITY CONTROL . The PM is responsible for oversight of all program activities. Our on-site management of the QCP will be assigned to a Quality Control Manager (QCM) who will report directly to the PM. This supervisory chain ensures the QCM can execute their responsibilities as an independent auditor and report their findings on the quality of program performance directly to NSI Corporate Quality leadership and/or to GSA leadership. The benefits of incorporating such detailed layers focused on quality ensure services are administered correctly and consistently throughout the project lifecycle. Factor Four: Project Experience Use or disclosure of data contained on this sheet is subject to the restriction on the title page of this proposal. National Security Innovations, Inc. Proprietary Information The US faces increasingly complex national security issues in every area of the globe that require research, studies, development and validation of tools, and analytic methodologies to enable decision -makers to pivot rapidly across a wide array of operational imperatives. NSI staff possess a broad range of analytic competencies, extensive expertise, and many years of hands -on experience conducting research and creating methodologies tailored to these issues. SMA is a multi -disciplinary, multi -agency portfolio of projects that assess and study challenging “hard problems” associated with planning and operations of DoD, military services, and Government agencies. SMA projects involve intense yet ﬁnite study periods of six- to nine -months where proof -of-concept and prototype capabilities are developed and applied to overcome challenges. An extensive network of leading researchers and practitioners participate in SMA, spanning the DoD, intelligence community, the interagency, universities, industry, and national laboratories. SMA research is accepted, prioritized, and synchronized by the J oint Staff/J -39 DDGO and executed b y the Under Secretary of Defense for Acquisition, Technology and Logistics (USD (AT&L)) through the Deputy Assistant Secretary of Defense for Emerging Capability & Prototyping (DASD EC&P)/Rapid Reaction Technology Office (RRTO). NSI supports SMA on project s ranging from nuclear non - proliferation on the Korean peninsula, the challenge of social unrest in emerging megacities, countering the emergent threat from ISIS, gray zone conﬂict from emerging near peers, and the challenges of competition in space. (2) Methodology, tools, and/or processes utilized in performing the work Our niche is helping clients better and more reliably understand people and their behaviors on critical, complex decision -making problems. Our capabilities are rooted in a highly diverse and experienced team of researchers and analysts applying multidisciplinary social science techniques and various analytic methods to create deeper analyses and clarifying insights enabling our clients to make more informed and better decisions. • Deeper Analyses: To create meaningful analyses one must move beyond asking “what happened” and instead ask “why it happened” and understand the conditions under which it might happen again. • Clarifying Insights: Data is abundant. Plots and graphs are easy. Insights are very hard. But when they are created, insights can be immensely powerful because they are actionable and create value for the client. • Better Decisions: Diversity provokes thought. Decades of research have shown that, for solving complex problems, diversity –a fundamental tenet of NSI –creates far better results than does homogeneity. NSI Organizational Chart ………………………………………………………………………………….22 3 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEExecutive Summary Gray Zones: Where we came from Understanding international affairs, and the optimum US strategy for dealing with them, is an evolutionary process that takes decades. In 1947, George Kennan wrote about containing the Soviet Union and communist expansion. Twenty-five years later Nixon and Kissinger revised containment to include détente with another communist country (China) as the best way to contain Russia, and during the 1980s, the Reagan Administration went about containment by way of defense spending and proxy warfare. The dissolution of the Soviet Union on the day after Christmas 1991, switched the strategic discussion in the US from containing Soviet global influence to defining the contours of the post-Cold War “new world order”, and characterizing the threats if any, to US interests that it posed. The debate continued for another ten years during which the US saw itself as the “sole superpower”, unchallenged militarily or economically by its nearest-peers. Ironically, it was a group of 19 individuals who ended US complacency in September 2001. What followed was nearly 20 years of military operations and supporting research first to understand, and then to craft strategies to counter radicalization, terrorism, and insurgency. The 2017 National Security Strategy and the subsequent 2018 National Defense Strategy) were the first since the 2001 attacks that did not include counter-terror as a significant defense priority. Instead, the documents turned US strategic attention to a turbulent international environment propelled by near-peers threatening US global interests. They did this not by projecting military power in conventional ways, but by employing “new” tactics in the “gray zone” or, more recently, the “competitive” zone. These include a rapidly expanding set of strategies and threats to US security interests that exceed acceptable competition but stay below the level of armed conflict. Gray Zone conflict lies between peace and war and manifests in constantly changing ways, creating the need for updated and evolving methodologies for preparing to meet these new and fluid challenges. Where we are Activities in the gray zone are by design ambiguous. It can be unclear who is responsible (e.g., media manipulation prior to the 2012 general election in the US); what the challenger’s ultimate objective may be (e.g., Chinese island building in the South China Sea) or even whether a challenge has taken place at all (e.g., Russian cyber efforts to spur civil conflict in Ukraine). However, one intention is clear: gray zone challenges are used to achieve a state’s objectives while frustrating US military or other punitive responses. There is not a single condition or definition that can distinguish an activity as within the “gray zone” independent of the geospatial and strategic contexts. Gray zone challenge can happen on multiple timescales, in different domains, in different locations, and on different levels of human society (e.g., global, regional, state, group and individual). The time scales are long and defy quick solutions to understand and counter. China has a much-touted 100-year strategy for world dominance, while the US works on four-year political cycles (Pillsbury 2015). Our strategic focus and supporting research must go beyond current frameworks. The combinations of these factors make for an operational setting that is extremely difficult to discern and understand, and poses a research problem that is intricately complex and non-deterministic and requires multiple iterations of multi-disciplinary and integrated solutions as well as geospatial customization to account for not only issues specific to different theater, but also capture nuances of likely responses from different population subgroups. 4 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEWhere we need to be US adversaries have been convinced of US dominance in conventional military maneuver. As a result, near-peer states in particular have turned to human cognition and affect, cultural beliefs, master narratives, ethnic identities, access to information, and economic dependencies as critical conflict domains. In order to protect and advance US security, US decision makers and planners need reliable, adaptive and accessible methods and tools to help them think about, identify, diagnose, and understand gray zone challenges within their geospatial contexts. They need means of assuring, deterring and defeating in areas beyond traditional military domains and tactics and means of devising appropriate responses rather than relying on kinetic solutions only, but by using tools that are developed for this specific and very new type of strategic thinking. Currently, few tools exist, creating a critical need for advanced research on how to predict, assess, and manage the inter-relationships between cognition and emerging trends within societies, as well as responses to specific peer gray zone activities. How to get there While there is a good deal of historical and contemporary information about gray zone activities there is as yet, very little empirically tested and evaluated, accumulated knowledge about the use of gray zone strategies to gain security advantage. This knowledge is essential to guide US planners and strategists in navigating the rapidly evolving 21st Century global order as it emerges. NSI proposes to enhance knowledge and understanding of gray zone challenges, generate methods for assessment, and aid in identifying and planning effective defense by pursuing research in line with core types of gray zone strategy, each of which can manifest on geo-spatial levels ranging from global to the mind of an individual. Together, these gray zone strategy types and geospatial levels produce four proposed gray zone research topics (threads) as shown in Figure 1. below. These are: Stability and Instability, Indirect and Hybrid Threats, Communication and Information Operations, and Gray Zone Ambiguity Reduction. NSI's depth of experience researching gray zone topics, and unique analytic approach to national security problems makes it particularly well-suited to advance gray zone research in line with these four threads. Furthermore, NSI’s multi-disciplinary staff has extensive expertise fusing social science disciplines to design and execute large, multi-stage, multi-team research programs and agendas that tackle national security problems. NSI’s proposed gray zone research program reflects our technical expertise as well as our experience. Leading the effort for NSI shall be Dr. Allison Astorino-Courtois, Executive VP and Chief Analytics Officer. Dr. Astorino-Courtois has over 15 years of experience in quantitative political science and decision theoretic research, including nearly 13 years as technical lead of national security research and analyses. Supporting Dr. Astorino-Courtois shall be a team of NSI analysts and researchers including Dr. Lawrence Kuznar, Chief Cultural Sciences Officer; Ms. Sarah Canna, Principal Analyst; and Ms. Mariah Yager, Senior Research Scientist. 5 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEVolume I – Technical Proposal 1.1 Technical Approach Despite our increasingly digital and virtual world, geography matters and as much for gray zone threats as for any others. Threats and opportunities play out in space; internet trolls operate out of specific locations (e.g., Macedonia, St. Petersburg), affecting people in other locations (France, Germany, Estonia, Ukraine), often producing broad geo-political impact. Supplying warfighters with the geographically sensitive knowledge they need requires innovative basic and applied research in geospatial and related sciences that characterize and measure phenomena across physical, cognitive, social, cyber, and ideological domains. These domains are overlapping and cross-cutting, no single domain has meaning outside its contextual relationship to others. Therefore, scientific approaches to understanding the interrelationships of these domains must include a suite of analytic methods and tools adaptable and tailorable to specific mission requirements in order to provide operators, analysts, strategists and decision makers a rich, contextual understanding of how physical, social, cultural and political factors play out in space. 1.2 Technical Discussion NSI's depth of experience researching gray zone topics and unique analytic approach to national security problems makes it particularly well-suited to advance gray zone understanding.1 Among other efforts, NSI has produced concept papers defining and validating operationalization of the gray zone concept, exploring transgression of international norms as a gray zone tactic, the gaps in US capability to counter gray zone activities that target the cognitive domain, and a series of case studies exploring the analytic power of discourse analysis for detecting gray zone strategies employed against the US. NSI has a unique, multi-disciplinary staff of researchers with extensive expertise in research design, hypothesis generation and in leveraging and creating analytic approaches across social science disciplines (i.e., human geography, anthropology, archeology, psychology, decision theory, international relations) to address topics of vital concern to the US national security community. NSI researchers also bring decades of combined experience executing large, multi-stage, multi-team research programs and agendas that tackle problems for which DOD lacks the necessary skills and intellectual networks to address appropriately. NSI’s proposed gray zone research program reflects our technical expertise as well as our experience working with Combatant Commanders and other senior DOD decision makers whose understanding of new types of challenges and conflict, and the implications for US policy and operations continues to evolve. In the following sections we first discuss the proposed substantive approach, and then briefly outline the foundations and process of NSI’s approach to research, analysis and transforming information into knowledge. 1 From 2016-2017, at the request of General Joseph Votel, NSI designed, participated in and executed one of the first research efforts to operationalize and test the concept of “gray zone warfare” put forward by Votel et al (2016). 6 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCESubstantive Approach to Gray Zone Research While there is a good deal of historical and contemporary information about gray zone activities there is as yet, very little, systematic concept development, or empirically tested and evaluated, accumulated knowledge about the use of gray zone strategies to gain security advantage. Unfortunately, there is a gap in the evidence-based knowledge essential to guide planners and strategists in navigating the rapidly evolving 21st Century global order as it emerges. This gap is the impetus for the proposed research program described below. NSI proposes to contribute to DOD understanding of gray zone challenges and conflict by undertaking a research program to produce refined analytic frameworks and prototype new methodologies specifically tailored to analysis of the gray zone environment. This is the core of the proposed research program. We use, the gray zone activities and strategies that planners and decision makers are most likely to face in the coming decade as an organizing structure (i.e., research agenda) for the proposed research We propose to conduct gray zone research in line with four of what we call gray zone research “threads” – or areas of knowledge. Each is described briefly below. • Stability and Instability Research Thread. Subverting political and economic stability in particular regions, particular states, or sub-state areas and populations has been used as a potent means for challenging US national interests, and/or achieving security gains at the expense of the US or its allies and partners short of the use of armed conflict. The importance of proximity and the contagion effects of instability are inherent geo-spatial aspects of this gray zone strategy. This is a gray zone strategy that has been used recently by Russia in Ukraine and Crimea. Understanding the stability Figure 1. NSI Gray Zone Research Program 7 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEand instability dynamics of a locality, or polity is essential for countering destabilization as a gray zone strategy. • Indirect and Hybrid Threat Research Thread. Use of proxy actors or other forms of indirect challenge and aggression are also important gray zone tactics. For example, Iran has long backed Hezbollah as a standing and sometimes active deterrent threat against Israeli and US aggression. Likewise, North Korea’s unclaimed cyber-attacks against US corporations are intended to communicate its power to injure the US while preserving the regime’s plausible deniability and hindering US retaliation. Enhancing US capabilities to discover and verify the provenance of indirect aggression against the US or its allies is essential both for deterrence of subsequent gray zone activities and the credibility of US conventional deterrence. • Communication and Information Operations Research Thread. Targeting popular perceptions of governments, elected officials, the US or other issues by manipulating social media, public access to local political information and generating fake news has emerged as a particularly insidious gray zone strategy. It is also an area in which the US struggles to keep pace with less legally-encumbered peer competitors. There is a serious US capability gap that requires significant research into cultural and geo-spatial contextual differences in receptivity to all forms of communication (word and action) intended to persuade. • Gray Zone Ambiguity Reduction Research Thread. Ambiguity about the features of the operational context is a key characteristic of the gray zone, and a strategy to promote ambiguity and uncertainty can be particularly difficult to counter. In order to understand and ideally, anticipate another state’s actions, analysts and decision makers require a systematic, transparent and robust set of techniques to better understand the incentives and constraints that impact that actor’s decision making. NSI Research Methodology and Process The US faces increasingly complex national security issues in every area of the globe that require research, studies, development and validation of tools, and analytic methodologies to enable decision-makers to pivot rapidly across a wide array of operational imperatives. NSI staff possess a broad range of analytic competencies, extensive expertise, and many years of hands-on experience conducting research and creating methodologies tailored to these issues. While the four research threads indicate what NSI proposes to work on, the following section describes how NSI works. All of NSI’s research projects are based in behavioral social science and founded in systematic analysis employing the scientific method as adapted to the study of human society. Our technical approach, is consciously multi-disciplinary and multi-method intended to assess a problem from many different perspectives in order to develop a contextual understanding that is as nuanced and complete as possible. As a consequence, NSI research efforts are comprised of four main phases as shown in Figure 2, Phase 1— arguably the most critical phase— consists of careful definition of the research problem or objective. The criticality of, and expertise required for successful completion of this phase is underappreciated. NSI staff have decades of experience doing precisely this kind of problem definition and scoping experience. Creating a research program or study entails a fairly consistent set of steps each of which rely on the previous ones, and ultimately the value of the research question posed. During Phase 2, the single or multi-team (generally representing relevant disciplines and methods) research design is constructed. Primary tasks in this phase include development of a fully-specified analytic frame to guide generation of hypotheses, operationalized definition of 8 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEresearch variables and the choice of analytical method(s) appropriate to the research question and observable (empirical) data. A carefully designed research effort leads the research team through the tasks necessary for successful completion. During Phase 3 NSI uses a number of data collection methods (e.g., global subject matter expert (SME) elicitation; theory and literature review; social media scraping; fusing of existing quantitative data sources; combing of historical records and cases, etc.). Hypotheses are tested and results evaluated per the design choices made during the previous phase. Analytical results are produced, and depending on the variety of methods used, findings from different components of the project are compared, validated and integrated. While coordination with other researchers and persistent internal review and revision occur throughout Phases 2 and 3, NSI adds an external review and evaluation step as Phase 4 to allow for community of practice peers and interested operator review to assure the analytic rigor and operational relevance of our studies. This can take many forms including scientific review groups, research presentations and conferences. Some of the techniques, models and methods that may be leveraged to support Phases 2-4 are elaborated below. Further Explanation of Phase 2 Execution The core of the proposed research is to develop concepts and methods applicable to the specific characteristics of operational environments in which gray zone strategies are used. Where appropriate, NSI will leverage earlier work done for the USG to understand gray zone concepts, and preliminary analytic frameworks (i.e., 6.1 research) for the proposed research. Specifically, NSI will test, refine, and evaluate Figure 3. Example Elements of a Gray Zone Research Project Figure 2. NSI Research, Development, Testing & Evaluation Process 9 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEthese for construct validity and as user-friendly tools for gray zone analyses. If no feasible method, framework or tool exists, NSI shall create, and conduct systematic tests to refine new approaches and methodologies tailored for analysis of gray zone activities. Many aspects of gray zone research are agnostic to specific local or international actor (i.e., the same gray zone research might be conducted on China, Hezbollah, or Togo). Thus, in order to provide the DoD and AGC with added value, NSI will accept suggestions of real-world, gray zone use cases offered by the Joint Staff to use in the process of the gray zone research program. This represents a novel approach to applied research that directs it toward use cases representing current operational problems and decisions. The government receives both the core research output (concepts, methods and tools for the gray zone), plus timely analyses of issues of critical operational importance in the process. Examples of initial behavioral analytic expertise, frameworks, approaches and methodologies that NSI has developed are described below. Stability Model-based Analytic Methodology (NSI-developed) NSI’s stability model and analytic methodology is guided by an adaptable generic model tailored to reflect the historical, cultural, social and political contexts and structures of a particular location. It has been used in research on stability and instability dynamics in Afghanistan, Nigeria, Pakistan, the Palestinian Authority, and post-ISIS Iraq. The formalized concept model allows analysts and researchers to systematically and transparently uncover drivers of instability and stability buffers (areas of resilience). Research within the Stability & Instability thread will be used to adapt this model to gray zone-specific problems and challenges, customize the framework within geospatial contexts, and improve the validity of the model. Statistical Modeling NSI employs advanced statistical analyses when appropriate to a research effort. National security problems are often complex and understanding them requires appropriate analysis of data that suffer from methodological weaknesses including incompleteness, multi-collinearity, uncertainty, nonlinearity, non-normality, etc. Several NSI staff members have decades of experience with advanced statistical methodologies designed to meet these data challenges. They have applied these methodologies in academic (Kuznar 1991, 2003), proprietary commercial, and government settings. For example, advanced imputation methods were combined with statistical modeling to provide characterization of the types of groups and global regions where nuclear and biological agents were most likely to be smuggled by terrorists (Kuznar et al, 2009), the outputs of which were used to produce geo-spatial heat maps to assist USSOCOM to better plan where to focus assets. Recently developed methodologies for handling multi-collinear independent variables were applied for revealing driving factors to state fragility, terrorism, and irregular migration, the results of which produced global heat maps of use for long-range strategic campaign planning. Figure 4. NSI Stability Model - Nigeria 10 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCESocial Network Analysis Modeling Social and geospatial connections influence the flow of information, the capability of actors, and overall dynamics of the complex battlespace. NSI, along with USG partners (TRADOC) developed social network analysis models of the complex alliances and enmities between state and non-state actors in the Middle East that produced metrics to gauge regional stability and to measure the relative political power of states, their proxies, and jihadist organizations (Kuznar & Astorino-Courtois, 2017). This research produced findings to support U.S. efforts to defeat ISIS and mitigate Russian and Iranian influence in the Middle East, and could easily be adapted to research within the Proxy and Indirect Aggression gray zone research. Quantitative Discourse Analysis NSI discourse analysis is particularly appliable to the Communication & IO Research Thread. It uncovers the underlying attitudes, biases, behavioral intentions, sentiment, and cultural assumptions in leaders’ speeches, population chatter, community feedback, social media commentary, and other forms of digitized communications. NSI applies multiple linguistic and thematic analysis techniques, fueled by text analytic software, to capture structure, patterns, rhetoric, and culturally relevant themes in large, unstructured corpora of discourse. The resulting quantitative data are then used to gauge values, intent, and commitment of leaders and stakeholders and to test hypotheses regarding adversary intent and courses of action. When applied in a regional context, the discursive patterns of many actors have been used to construct the geo-spatial network of alliances while social network analysis has been employed to reveal levels of instability and key actors. Some recent applications included: Assessment of the strategic perspective of Bashar al Assad, the strategic and operational objectives of ISIS (Kuznar, 2017), Russian objectives in Eurasia, Russian and Chinese objectives in outer space, and North Korean Leadership Worldview, and post-summit assessments. NSI proposes to adapt these methodologies to gray zone use cases, and use them to develop methodologies for ongoing monitoring of related discourse, both social and geo-political. However, the rapidly changing nature of these communication themes will require development of adaptive models and application of multi-faceted social and behavioral science. Figure 5. NSI Middle East Network Model Figure 6. NSI Discourse Analysis Methodology 11 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEAI/Machine Learning for Natural Language Processing (NLP) NSI uses artificial intelligence and machine learning for automatically identifying and categorizing interests from a variety of text-based sources. In the last iteration, significant progress was made in separating out auto-detected interests from a broad corpus without the need for extensive operator manipulation of data. Interest-Resolve-Capability (I-R-C) Regional Dynamics Analysis Methodology (NSI-developed) NSI developed its I-R-C analysis as a systematic method for exploring the complex, multi-actor, multi-interest relationships and dynamics that determine one or another regional future. It assesses these forces according to the confluences of three factors that condition state and/or non-state behaviors: 1) actors’ interests are the security, political, social, economic, and influence interests that an actor perceives to be at stake in a given context; 2) the actors’ relevant capability refers to the ability to directly influence or cause a particular outcome to occur; and, 3) actors’ resolve—the intent or willingness to do so. An I-R-C analysis produces a decision and interests analysis (see below), an empirical measure of resolve, and an assessment of each actors’ relative capabilities in relation to specific outcomes or events. The I-R-C methodology has been applied to the Levant and Gulf region, and the Western Pacific region. NSI proposes conducting research regarding adapting the I-R-C model to a variety of current and emerging gray zone dynamics, customized within geospatial contexts. Decision and Interest Analysis (NSI-developed) Issues that prompt decision calculations are comprised of three elements: 1) the options for action an actor believes he/she has; 2) the dimensions (concerns, interests) that determine preferences among those options; and 3) what each actor believes other relevant actors will do (i.e., the options and preferences attributed to others, in some cases including the state of nature (Astorino-Courtois, 1995, 2000, Bienenstock & Astorino-Courtois 2011). NSI has used its cognitive decision theory-based, subjective decision approach to create systematic “reconstructions” of interest-based (political, social, cultural, identity, international influence and prestige, and economic) decision calculi from the perspective of various actors of interest. The resulting analysis uncovers the range of possible “influence levers” for assuring an ally, or dissuading or deterring unacceptable activities by an opponent, as well as the strategies and influence points most likely to be most effective. This analytic technique has been applied in multiple studies and has produced well-researched and vetted individual “actor interest reports” including those on Egypt, Iran, Iraq, Russia, Saudi Arabia, and Syria. Further Explanation of Phase 3 Execution NSI also has developed and will leverage unique data collection techniques for testing its models against empirical data, including: Figure 7. NSI I-R-C Analysis 12 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCENSI’s Virtual Think Tank (ViTTa®) subject matter expert (SME) elicitation ViTTa efforts begin with pulsing an extensive list of vetted, US and international academic and think tank subject matter experts (SMEs) to generate data for other project needs (e.g., to support computational models, war games, etc.). In order preserve the raw data, NSI asks chosen SMEs to provide written submissions or, if preferred, NSI conducts a recorded 30-60-minute telephone interview. A ViTTa summary report or more in-depth Reachback Report may serve as an interim deliverable of the ongoing research project. Publications Repository For the same reasons, NSI has built an extensive, web-based repository of publications that provides a rich source of geospatial and analytic data. This repository includes over 200 government-sponsored research and analysis publications addressing a wide range of challenging national security problems and operational imperatives written between 2007 and the present. New research will, as appropriate, leverage data and conclusions from relevant past publications and reports. Automated data collection and updating NSI has extensive data science experience with automatically accessing “big data” sources, creating databases tailored to customer and government research needs, and updating these products. This capability will be essential to the proposed research to provide analysts and commanders the timely and accurate geospatial awareness they need for decision making. Further Explanation of Phase 4 Execution International relations, such as gray zone challenges, not only deals with complex systems of systems that shape human behaviors, it involves concepts and strategies for which it can be impossible to build prototypes that can be tested in the real world in real time. There are two reasons for this: 1) the act of researching or testing a particular subject’s behavior changes or adds error to an analysis; and 2) the costs in human lives, political opinion, safety, etc. of doing so are too dear. It is of course unreasonable and immoral to start a war in order to study specific aspects of wartime behavior. As a result, in the social sciences research presentations and peer-review of interim findings, novel concepts or new analytic approaches are a crucial tool in evaluating the scientific foundation, feasibility and practicality of research output. NSI has a number of means of disseminating research in order to elicit critical review from peer researchers as well as operators likely to be interested in, and use, the information produced. These include both written and oral presentation of key concepts and methodologies, in this case to the substantial SMA community of interests, including via: Publications NSI staff provide original research and expert contributions to government journals and white papers as well as peer-reviewed academic publications (e.g. Astorino-Courtois & Kuznar 2011). SMA White Papers Figure 8. NSI Virtual Think Tank (ViTTa) Process 13 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEin particular provide valuable input into the research process by gathering different perspectives and efforts into a unified document, and providing feedback necessary for evaluating the validity and usefulness of NSI research efforts. The weekly SMA newsletter also features scholarly publications on topics of interest to the SMA community related to current research efforts. It shall be distributed worldwide to over 5000 members of the SMA community of interest, including DoD, whole of government, think tanks, academia, and foreign allies, in order to more effectively disseminate findings, share important research developments, and invite input. Speaker Sessions NSI vets the bona fides of distinguished scholars and practitioners to speak for the purpose of gaining awareness of the landscape of perspectives and research on key topics of interest. The purpose of the speaker series is to serve as an audio journal through which researchers and government personnel can tap into the collective knowledge base and engage in discussion and debate about on-going research and analyses among the federal inter-agency, universities, and others. NSI records and posts these events to a central repository accessible by other researchers, warfighters and reviewers. These sessions provide invaluable input and opportunities for discussion on a variety of gray zone related issues, thereby better informing the overall research process. Research Presentations at Research Symposium NSI makes presentations on research findings at a Joint Staff J39-hosted research symposium that addresses science and technology research and development related to national security threats and solutions. In addition, NSI identifies subject matter experts to make presentations, and suggests speaker topics in general. The symposium is attended by interested members of academia, government, and the private sector. It provides a unique marketplace for researchers and Combatant Commands to review and respond to research efforts that have produced interim or final results over the previous year. Participation in this two-day conference has risen steadily to reach over 300 attendees each year. This event is a helpful component of the evaluation of the scientific validity, reasonableness and instrumental value to end users of the proposed research. It will also provide NSI researchers with guides for anticipating future use cases, hypotheses, data requirements, and methodological developments needed to address emerging and undiscovered gray zone challenges. It should be noted that the Symposium is a no-fee event and thus there are no facility or other ODC costs associated with NSI’s presenting its research there (only minimal travel costs and time spent attending.) There are no expectations that government personnel will provide, or be assigned to provide, review. It is done as a social convention of the community of scholars. Government personnel participate in the conference and community review of research as their interest determines. In addition, given current uncertainty concerning the possibility of travel and larger meetings in the coming months, in the event that the Symposium is cancelled, NSI will lean more heavily on Publications and Speaker Sessions to conduct external, peer review and pulse expert reviewers via other modes of communication and review. 1.2.1 Research Outcomes and Associated Products There are two fundamental outcomes from the proposed multilevel, multimethod research efforts: 1) findings that refine understanding of gray zone concepts, challenges and possible US responses; and 2) creation and revision of analytic frameworks, tools and methodologies for conducting gray zone-specific analysis. The proposed NSI effort will expand the domain of scientific knowledge with regard to gray zone challenges. The expanded knowledge from all NSI research efforts will be captured in integration reports and reside in a government-owned archive. In addition, NSI puts its own and other analytic frameworks 14 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEthrough a rigorous cycle of testing to uncover flaws and indicate improvements. The result is improved representations of the world, that in turn improve the accuracy of analyses. This has been a constant endeavor at NSI. All frameworks and methods will be subject to a critical evaluation and revised accordingly to improve the state-of-the-art of gray zone science. A number of concrete products are generated from these outcomes, including technical reports, multimedia presentations, and computational, machine learning and statistical models. 1.2.2 Research Coordination Research project management and support is essential for project success. Working with coordinating and integrating the work of multiple sub-teams that may use different research methods, different or sometimes shared databases, and across security domains is a daunting task. NSI shall synchronize and integrate the output of its own and other contributors’ research on gray zone efforts. Research management activities also include management of all security requirements for researcher access to government resources, meetings and protection of classified sources and information that may be accessed as part of a research project. In addition, NSI shall help assure the scientific validity and success of the research project with a weekly teleconference with other researchers. 1.3 Technical Program Summary As was just described, NSI shall produce a broad array of gray zone research in coordination with AGC and the SMA program. To mitigate this risk, NSI utilized a formal integration stage within its various multi-method and multidisciplinary efforts in order to find consistencies, and resolve inconsistencies, across different work streams and disciplines. NSI shall implement a Quality Control Program (QCP) for this effort. Volume II describes the framework and processes within the QCP for delivering quality products and services required by the tasks in this effort. This quality control plan shall be provided to the Government within ten (10) days after contract award. NSI shall provide a briefing to the Government outlining the plan for implementation of the QCP for the contract tasks during the kick-off meeting. NSI shall ensure all work will be performed in accordance with the contract requirements and the quality control plan. NSI shall provide the requisite staffing and procedures to meet the quality, quantity, timeliness, responsiveness, customer satisfaction, and service delivery and performance requirements of this effort. NSI shall identify in the QCP, the applicable processes and metrics used to self-assess performance in addition to the resources to be applied to this effort. 1.5 References Astorino-Courtois, A., & Kuznar, L.
