Our niche is helping clients better and more reliably understand people and their behaviors on critical, complex decision-making problems. Our capabilities are rooted in a highly diverse and experienced team of researchers and analysts applying multidisciplinary social science techniques and various analytic methods to create deeper analyses and clarifying insights enabling our clients to make more informed and better decisions. • Deeper Analyses: To create meaningful analyses one must move beyond asking “what happened” and instead ask “why it happened” and understand the conditions under which it might happen again. • Clarifying Insights: Data are abundant. Plots and graphs are easy. Insights are very hard. But when they are created, insights can be immensely powerful because they are actionable and create value for the client. • Better Decisions: Diversity provokes thought. Decades of research have shown that, for solving complex problems, diversity–a fundamental tenet of NSI–creates far better results than does homogeneity. 2.2 Capabilities and Relevant Experience Since its founding, NSI has worked on hundreds of projects for government and commercial clients. Our clients have become increasingly aware of the importance of accounting for the human component in their analytical and decision-making processes. However, many of their existing practices do not sufficiently accommodate such considerations. Helping clients understand people and their behaviors is precisely what we do. Below is a sample of NSI’s relevant experience. To see a much more expansive list, visit our website at www.nsiteam.com. Strategic Multi-Layer Assessment (SMA) SMA is a multi-disciplinary, multi-agency portfolio of projects that assess and study challenging “hard problems” associated with planning and operations of DoD, military services, and Government agencies. SMA projects involve intense yet finite study periods of six- to nine-months where proof-of-concept and prototype capabilities are developed and applied to overcome challenges. An extensive network of leading researchers and practitioners participate in SMA, spanning the DoD, intelligence community, the interagency, universities, industry, and national laboratories. SMA research is accepted, prioritized, and synchronized by the Joint Staff/J-39 DDGO and executed by the Under Secretary of Defense for Acquisition, Technology and Logistics (USD (AT&L)) through the Deputy Assistant Secretary of Defense for Emerging Capability & Prototyping (DASD EC&P)/Rapid Reaction Technology Office (RRTO). NSI has supported the Government in formulating, executing, and providing analyses for numerous SMA projects to date. In 2007, NSI coordinated modeling and analysis efforts for two projects: Sudan Strategic Assessment, which provided CENTCOM with an assessment of the Sudan and Horn of Africa by applying quantitative and computational social science models that addressed three concerns: (i) root causes of the humanitarian crisis, (ii) regional effects Sudan is having on the Horn of Africa, and (iii) conditions that are causing Sudan to become a safe haven for nefarious activity. In 2007 and 2009, NSI also designed coordinated two Deterrence projects, which focused on providing STRATCOM with a strategic deterrence framework (methodology) for 21st century state and non-state threats. These projects explored the utility 17 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEof wargaming and modeling to improve the analytic foundation of strategic deterrence planning, identified elements of strategic deterrence aptly analyzed through wargaming and various sorts of modeling, and defined methods to apply wargaming and modeling to deterrence planning processes. In 2008, NSI led the modeling effort for the JIPOE (Joint Intelligence Preparation of the Operational Environment) project where SOCOM was provided with a detailed statistical analysis of two WMD-T case studies: one focused on nuclear smuggling in the Caucuses and Southern Asian region and the other focused on bio terrorism. In 2008-09, NSI led multiple aspects of the Inter-agency Limited Objective Experiment (IA LOE), which was focused on evaluating state-of-the-art modeling and analysis tools to help analysts anticipate rare events, measuring and demonstrating the value of collaborative processes, enabling tools and environments, and network architectures to find and characterize leading indicators of rare events. In 2009-10, NSI coordinated a major initiative for the ISAF Headquarters to provide the ISAF commander a rich contextual understanding of the Afghanistan/Pakistan region. Since then, NSI has supported SMA on projects ranging from nuclear non-proliferation on the Korean peninsula, the challenge of social unrest in emerging megacities, countering the emergent threat from ISIS, gray zone conflict from emerging near peers, and the challenges of competition in space, much of which has been cited in the above task descriptions. Socio-cultural Geo-informatics Lab (SGIL) In the Socio-cultural Geo-informatics Lab (SGIL) program, NSI built a state-of-the-art socio-cultural geo-informatics testbed to support assessment, test and evaluation (T&E), and transitioning of Human Social Culture Behavior Modeling (HSCB) technologies. In order to support OSD’s HSCB modeling initiative, NSI collaborated with Government, industry, FFRDCs, and academic partners to perform validation and applied research, early testing and transition of prototypes, maturing and hardening of testbed, T&E of HSCB models, and specification of metrics. During 2008, NSI built core infrastructure within the Army Geospatial Center’s Joint Geospatial Enterprise Services (JGES) facility, designed a socio-cultural data collection approach, and developed a GeoWiki as well as an agent-based civil unrest Thai software prototype in AnyLogic. During 2009, NSI provided test & assessment support for HSCB, helped to build sociocultural T&E and metrics framework, and designed basic structure for Technical Integration Experiments (TIEs). Mapping the Human Terrain (MAP-HT) The objective of the MAP-HT Joint Concept Technology Demonstration (JCTD) program was to develop, integrate, test, evaluate, and transition a socio-cultural toolkit to consolidate, visualize, and understand open source socio-cultural data to assist Commanders in understanding the “human terrain” in which they operate. The program sought to provide a relevant joint common picture of the socio-cultural human terrain for use by tactical elements, operational commanders, theater planners, interagency organizations, and coalition partners. The initial phase of MAP-HT contained early, accelerated transitions of various spirals of the socio-cultural toolkit to the Human Terrain System (HTS) program; the longer-term focus was on transitioning to DCGS-A/HDWS (Distributed Common Ground Station—Army/Human Domain WorkStation). The various sponsors and stakeholders included CENTCOM, Army Corps of Engineers Research and Development Center Topographic Engineering Center (ERDC-TEC), and DCGS-A. NSI served as a technical advisor to the program manager as well as provided a technology assessment of candidate technologies for various spirals of the socio-cultural toolkit. HumanGeo: Lazarus NSI staff worked as part of a multidisciplinary team to provide oversight of full analytical processes and technical performance evaluations of geospatial capabilities for the National Geospatial Intelligence 18 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEAgency (NGA). In addition to oversight, NSI staff provided social science expertise to compliment geospatial and all source intelligence analysis. The analytical processes developed included question formation, hypothesis development, data gathering, and analysis. Technological development included assessment of the software necessary for analysis and ultimate visualization as data, to include static representations up to interactive dashboards for nominal end users. Technologies tested and assessed included GOTS and COTS tools of interest to NGA. NSI contributed to the evaluation, design, and workflow, and produced notional analytical products representative of intelligence products. NSI assisted in developing procedures for systematically incorporating unclassified research across classified domains. Key activities included review and evaluation of software, data gathering and research, final product delivery, and evaluation reports. Results were briefed to various stakeholders, including military operators, intelligence analysts, contractors, and NGA officials including the Director and Deputy-Director. Gray Zone Conflicts Challenges and Opportunities United States Special Operations Command (USSOCOM) requested a Strategic Multi-layer Assessment effort “to determine how the USG can identify, diagnose, and assess indirect strategies, and develop response options against associated types of gray zone conflicts.” This integration report provided a synthesis of all the team projects. Their work advanced understanding of the contours of the gray zone terrain, and the challenges inherent in navigating that terrain. By identifying the critical features of the gray zone, the findings also provided a guide to where USSOCOM and other DoD entities should focus future efforts in this area to facilitate the development of operational level planning and response strategies. The key results of the effort fall into four areas summarized as follows: • What is the nature of gray zone conflict? There is no single condition that can identify an action as gray, independent of actor or understanding of the broader strategic context. We need to think on multiple timescales, across multiple arenas (e.g., political, social, economic), and understand and engage with multiple social levels (state, group, individual). Populations are the key dimensions in gray zone conflict. Norm violations help define the threshold between ordinary competition and the gray zone. • What motivates actors to engage in gray zone activities? Successful US deterrence has not eliminated the motivations of other actors to further their own interests. Acting in the gray zone is an effective low risk, low cost strategy that has proven difficult for US and partner nations to counter and for vulnerable states to defend against. US military places primacy on physical maneuver, and our adversaries know this. • How should the US respond to gray zone activities? It should incorporate the human/cognitive domain: think and plan beyond kinetic responses alone; expand DoD definitions of maneuver and objective to account for the human aspects of military operations; and shape the international environment to reduce the motivations for engaging in gray zone activities. It should also develop a clear, compelling strategic narratives: provide alternative narratives and leverage social and mass media to communicate them; build trust and credibility with partner nations to enable unity of effort; and an enduring, proactive presence and consistent messaging across all USG agencies is a significantly superior approach to taking select actions in response to specific gray actions. Scope and timing of US response matters: Inaction in the face of low-level actions (e.g. Chinese Island building in the SCS) can over time create a “new reality” that threatens US interests and security, and early and effective response to gray actions and strategies requires a consistent US presence. • What capabilities does the US need to respond effectively to gray zone activities? Human/Cognitive Domain Information & Expertise–Gray zone strategies exploit multiple instruments of power. Operating in this environment requires information across all of these instruments. Conceptual 19 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCEModels and Frameworks–The scope of gray zone activities will make information requirements overwhelming without models to guide search and interpretation. 2.3 Previous or Current Relevant Independent Research and Development (IR&D) Work This proposal has not been submitted to any other agency. NSI is currently engaged in an internal research and development project to develop machine learning and artificial intelligence automated algorithms to identify, code, and classify “interests” of state and non-state actors. The intent is to develop a capability to quickly find and help to facilitate leveraging of critical information in a rapid and comprehensive fashion, without the need for extensive manual searching of relevant material. Initial progress is very encouraging, with a stable separation of interest and non-interest coding of documents in the training data set. 2.4 Related Government Contracts A sample of POC’s for past performance is provided below. NSI will assure that each Thread is addressed at least once over the course of the 60-month contract period, and will make every effort at the design stage to incorporate more than one Thread per project. At the project overview level, each of what will amount to approximately seven research projects will be structured in accordance with NSI’s four-phase approach, and will include: • a 1-2 month problem definition phase to clearly specify the research question, identify key constructs, and define the problem scope (Phase I) • a 1-2 month research design phase including development of a fully-specified analytic frame, definition of concepts, operationalized definition of research variables and the choice of analytical method (Phase 2) • a 3-8 month hypothesis testing, data collection and analysis phase (Phase 3) Figure 9. Proposed GZ Research Timeline 21 NSIRESEARCH ▪ INNOVATION ▪ EXCELLENCE• and, and a 1-3 month phase for initial dissemination and peer review (Phase 4). Given the nature of the external review-revision-review process during Phase 4, the final integrated reports will have gone through multiple drafts. To avoid external reviewers holding up timely delivery of the final products to the government, NSI will release, as a proven best practice, findings from completed project sub tasks prior to the final review period. A Note on Why NSI Projects are so Complex The basis of NSI’s analytic philosophy, and our approach to wickedly complex problems such as gray zone challenges, is what we call “triangulation.” The concept of triangulating input to gain a more accurate perspective on a single point guides how we design and execute research projects (i.e., Phases 2 and 3). Specifically, we design our projects to combine input from multiple individual efforts, or sub-tasks, (usually, between five and twelve per single project.) These sub-tasks use multiple data sources and types of quantitative, qualitative and computational analyses to a single question or topic. For example, in the project shown in Figure 10, we engaged three different types of polling which provided data input for eight different types of analysis. Figure 11 shows the flowchart for a different project. While NSI’s analytic philosophy certainly adds complexity and breadth to our projects, looking at a problem from multiple angles provides the analytic rigor that makes our research findings both nuanced and robust. In addition, Phase 4 peer review is not limited to the final integrated project report. Individual sub-tasks report their own conclusions, and these are exposed to review by academics, interested members of the community of practitioners and others in the same ways that the integrated project reports are. For this reason, a typical “single” project will produce multiple reports of sub-task results as well as a single, vetted integration report that pulls the main narrative from the various sub-task reports. It is important to note that Integrating multiple research outputs does not mean finding the ‘least common denominator’ or forcing agreement: If sub-tasks produce different views this is reported (and further research is conducted to understand the source of the difference. Consensus views are held to a stricter standard. 3.2 Time Line Chart by Task For all projects as part of this effort, NSI shall follow a task deliverable schedule consistent with the table below. Customer/Client Name: Booz Allen Hamilton (BAH) – Prime AFRICOM Project Name/Contract Number: SUBCONTRACT A44909 Customer Point of Contact (POC) for Project: Ray Dow , Sr. Subcontract Administrator POC's Current Phone Number and Email: 303-563-3611 , Hendricks_Sandra @bah.com Project Performance Period (include months/years): 12/4/2023 – 9/5/2024 (Base) 9/6/2024 – 9/5/2027 Dollar Value of the Entire Project: $2M Dollar Value Received for the Work Performed Relevant to the SIN(s) Offered: $755,236 Brief Summary of Project: The operating environment (OE) in Africa is both complicated and complex. It results from the interplay of a staggering array of social, economic, and political factors, as well as changing physical and technological landscapes. USAFRICOM must be able to operate effectively in the environment that includes serious challenges wrought by the effects of climate change. The physical effects of global climate change include rapidly rising ground temperatures, devastating rises on sea levels and ocean temperatures, increased heavy precipitation (heavy rain and hail) and desertiﬁcation. However, the cascading effects of cli mate changes on human political, social, and economic security can be wide -ranging and extreme. In Africa these highly interdependent effects are already increasing the likelihood of complex security challenges: • Rising seas increase the salinity of ground water which can create food insecurity • Food insecurity and famine make populations more vulnerable to malign actors, and likely to migrate away from homes that have become unlivable • Large population migrations can stress infrastructure and services, and foment political and social instability in urban areas • Political and social tensions challenge weak and still -developing governing institutions and security sectors, increasing state fragility and instability that can easily bleed over from one country to another. Proprietary Information Alone, each of these concerns impacts the ability of the US to achieve national goals in Africa. Taken together they present an operating picture that may seem nearly intractable. Complete and accurate analyses of this context requires that the system -of-systems that these and other factors create is accounted for. (1) Detailed description of SIN relevant work performed and results achieved The proposed effort extends the work completed in AFOE phases I and II. It addresses the requirement by a) continu ing SMA analytic reach -back support of USAFRICOM decision -makers, planners and assessors demonstrated by the AFOE project, b) reﬁning the model to extend the scope of AECM to include climate and climate change impacts and improve its usefulness an analytic tool; and, c) providing training on the mindset and processes that will aid AFRICOM analysts in using the AECM most effectively . The task ar eas described below will be prioritized and relative levels -of-effort established following consultation with USAFRICOM. TASK 1: Analytic Reach- back Support . Reach -back support includes: • Quick Looks: Quick Look reports will be prepared on AECM sub -systems around nodes and topics as requested by or in consultation with USAFRICOM. • On request Consultation: The team will be available for additional consultation on model insights, data availability and other issues of concern relating to the AECM. TASK 2: AECM Reﬁnement: AECM reﬁnement consists of several tasks intended to increase the robustness of the model as well as its functionality for issues of greatest interest to USAFRICOM. These include: • Node & Sub -system Research . Owing to the period of performance of the AFOE effort, there are nodes and edges in the AECM that require additional node deﬁnition and exploration of edge relationships to increase conﬁdence in model validity especially on topics of particular concern to the Command like governing stability, and climate change. This sub -task may also include adding nodes or system modules (e.g., US -China competition) into the model. • Logic model Build -out. At present the AECM model is represented in an adjacency matrix that shows direct and cascades of indirect relationships between nodes. It does not however capture dependent or contingent relationships. The logic model allows experimentation to explore sy stem effects of perturbations with varied initial conditions. • AECM State -Level. Tailor AECM for regional, state -level, or sub -state levels, or to topics of interest topics (e.g., terrorism), with or without additional Quick Looks . TASK 3: Training . At the Government’s request, GECM/AECM training will include in -person, on - line, or hybrid four -day courses to provide AFRICOM users with an introduction to analytic and systems thinking via the GECM and AECM system -of-systems including how these models are created, what kinds of questions the model is suited to explore, and the limitations of this powerful method. The course may also include how to create Quick Looks and the use of data resources speciﬁc to the African continent. Training task activities will include course preparation, creation of course materials, and course delivery. AAMMEERRIICCAANNSS WWIITTHH DDIISSAABBIILLIITTIIEESS AACCTT PPOOLLIICCYY The Americans wit h Disabilities Act (ADA) requires an employer to provide reasonable accommodations for individuals with disabilities, unless it would cause undue hardship. A reasonable accommodation is any change in the work environment or in the way a job is performed th at enables a person with a disability to enjoy equal employment opportunities. If you require an accommodation you must inform your supervisor that there is a need for an adjustment or change at work for a reason related to a medical condition. We will respond promptly and to the best of our ability to accommodate the needs of all employees . CCLLAASSSSIIFFIICCAATTIIOONNSS OOFF EEMMPPLLOOYYMMEENNTT PPOOLLIICCYY For purposes of salary admin istration and eligibility for overtime payments and employment benefits, NSI classifies its employees as follows: − Full-time Regular: Employees hired to work NSI’s normal, full time, 30 hour or more workweek on a regular basis. Such employees may be “ exemp t” or “non -exempt” as defined below. − Part-time Regular: Employees hired to work fewer than 30 hours p er week on a regular basis. Such employees may be “exempt” or “non -exempt” as defined below. − Temporary: Employees engaged to work full time or part time on NSI’s payroll with the understanding that their employment will be terminated no later than upon com pletion of a specific assignment. (Note that a temporary employee may be offered, and may accept, a new temporary assignment with NSI and thus still retain temporary status.) Such employees may be “exempt” or “non-exempt” as defined below. (Note that emplo yees hired from temporary employment agencies for specific assignments are employees of the respective agency and not of NSI.) − Non-exempt: Employees who ar e required to be paid minimum wage and overtime at the federal or state prescribed wage rate, whichev er is higher. − Exempt: Employees who are not required to be paid minimum wage and overtime, in accordance with applicable federal wage and hour laws, for wo rk performed beyond forty hours in a workweek. Executives, professional employees, outside sales repr esentatives, certain computer programmers and employees in some administrative positions are typically exempt. Policies and Procedures Page 8 of 74 www.NSIteam .com PPOOLLIICCYY NNOO.. 000022:: EEMMPPLLOOYYEEEE CCOONNDDUUCCTT AANNTTII--HHAARRAASSSSMMEENNTT PPOOLLIICCYY It is the policy of NSI to maintain a working environment that encourages mutual respect, promotes respectful and congenial relationships between employees and that is free from all forms of harassment by anyone, including supervisors, co -workers, vendors, or customers. Harassment, even when not unlawful or directed at a protected category, is expressly prohibited and will not be tolerated. Accordingly, NSI management is committed to vigorous ly addressing complaints of harassment and sexual harassment at all levels. Reported or suspected occurrences of harassment will be promptly and thoroughl y investigated. Following an investigation, NSI will immediately take any necessary and appropriate d isciplinary action. NSI will not permit or condone any acts of retaliation against anyone who files harassment complaints or cooperates in the investigati on of same. 1. The term “harassment ” includes harassment based on any category protected by federal, st ate, or local law, which may include depending on the jurisdiction, but is not limited to, unwelcome slurs, jokes, or verbal, graphic or physical conduct r elating to an individual's race, color, religious creed, sex, national origin, ancestry, citizenship status, pregnancy, physical disability, mental disability, age, military status or status as a Vietnam -era or special disabled veteran, marital status, registered domestic partner or civil union status, gender (including sex stereotyping and gender identit y or expression), medical condition (including, but not limited to, cancer related or HIV/AIDS related) or sexual orientation . 2. Sexual harassment consists o f unwelcome sexual advances, requests for sexual favors, or other verbal or physical conduct of a sex ual nature where : a. Submission to such conduct is an explicit or implicit term or condition of employment ; b. Employment decisions are based on an employee's su bmission to or rejection of such conduct; or c. Such conduct interferes with an individual's work perfor mance or creates an intimidating, hostile or offensive working environment . Complaint Procedure NSI provides its employees with a convenient and reliable method for reporting incidents of harassment, including sexual harassment. Any employee who feels har assed or discriminated against is encouraged to immediately inform the alleged harasser that the behavior is unwelcome. In many instances, the person is unaware that their conduct is offensive and when so advised can easily and willingly correct the conduc t so that it does not reoccur. If the informal discussion with the alleged harasser is unsuccessful in remedying the problem, or if you do not feel comfort able with such an approach, you should immediately report the conduct to your immediate supervisor . Additionally, you should submit a written report of the problem to the head of Human Resources. We cannot help resolve a harassment problem unless we know a bout it. Therefore, it is your responsibility to bring those kinds of problems to our attention so th at we can take the necessary steps to correct the problem. The written report to the head of Human Resources should include all facts available to the empl oyee regarding the harassment or sexual harassment . Confidentiality All reports of harassment or sex ual harassment will be treated seriously. However, absolute confidentiality is not promised nor can it be assured. NSI will conduct an investigation of any complaint of harassment or sexual harassment, which may require limited disclosure of pertinent info rmation to certain parties, including the alleged harasser. Investigative Procedure NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 9 of 74 www.NSIteam .com Once a complaint of harassment or sexual harassment is received, NSI will begin a prompt and thorough investigation. The investigation may include interviews with all invo lved employees, including the alleged harasser, and any employees who are aware of facts or incidents alleged to have occurred. Following an investigation , NSI will immediately take any necessary and appropriate disciplinary action. Disciplinary action will be taken if the investigation reveals that an employee has acted in a manner that is not in alignment with the goal of this policy, even when the action s may be lawful. In fact, NSI may address any workplace issue discovered during an investigation. This may include some or all of the following steps: 1. Restore any lost terms, conditions or benefits of employment to the complaining employee. 2. Discipline the harasser. This discipline can include written disciplinary warnings, transfer, demotion, suspension, and termination . If the harassment or sexual harassment is from a vendor or customer the first step you should take is to notify NSI in writing. Submit the written report to the head of Human Resources. NSI will take appropriate action notify the vendor /customer of the situation and work with them to stop the conduct. As a result of NSI intervention, the vendor or customer may need to open an investigatio n of its own. Whenever an outside organization wants to interview your or attempts to obtain any deta ils from you regarding harassment that has happened in the workplace, a representative from NSI’s Human Resources must be present. Duties of Employees and Supervisors All employees of NSI , both management and non- management, are responsible for assuring t hat a workplace free of harassment or sexual harassment is maintained. Any employee may file a harassment complaint regarding incidents experienced persona lly or incidents observed in the workplace. NSI strives to maintain a lawful, pleasant work environme nt where all employees are able to effectively perform their work without interference of any type and requests the assistance of all employees in this effort. All NSI supervisors and managers are expected to adhere to the anti -harassment policy. Supervis ors' evaluations may include an assessment of the supervisor's efforts in following and enforcing this policy. All managers and supervisors are responsibl e for doing all they can to prevent and discourage harassment or sexual harassment from occurring. If a complaint of harassment or sexual harassment is raised, supervisors and managers are to act promptly and notify NSI Executive staff to proceed with an i nvestigation. If a supervisor or manager fails to follow this policy, he or she will be disciplined. Such discipline may include termination . GGUUIIDDEELLIINNEESS FFOORR AAPPPPRROOPPRRIIAATTEE CCOONNDDUUCCTT NSI employees are expected to accept certain responsibilities, follow acceptab le business principles in matters of conduct, and exhibit a high degree of integrity and ethical cond uct at all times. This not only involves sincere respect for the rights and feelings of others, but also demands that employees refrain from any behavior t hat might be harmful to themselves, co -workers, the company, or that might be viewed unfavorably by c urrent or potential customers or by the public at large. Employee conduct reflects on NSI. Employees are, consequently, encouraged to observe the highest s tandards of professionalism at all times. Types of behavior and conduct that NSI considers inappropr iate include, but are not limited to, the following: − Falsifying employment or other NSI records; − Violating NSI’s anti- harassment policy; − Soliciting or acc epting gratuities from customers or clients; Excessive absenteeism or tardiness; − Excessive, unnece ssary, or unauthorized use of NSI property and supplies, particularly for personal purposes; − Reporting to work under the influence of drugs or alcohol, and the illegal manufacture, possession, use, sale, distribution or transportation of drugs; NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 10 of 74 www.NSIteam .com − Unauthorize d use of alcoholic beverages on NSI property or using alcoholic beverages while engaged in NSI business off the company's premises, except where authorized ; − Fighting or using obscene, abusive, or threatening language or gestures; − Theft of property from co -workers, customers, or the company; − Unauthorized possession of firearms on NSI premises or while on NSI business; − Disregarding safety or security regulatio ns especially as regards classified materials and locations; and − Failing to maintain the confidentiality of NSI, customer, or client information. Should an employee’s performance, work habits, overall attitude, conduct or demeanor become unsatisfactory ba sed on violations either of the above or of any other NSI policies, rules, or regulations, the employ ee will be subject to disciplinary action, up to and including termination. Other behaviors resulting in a US Government security censure on NSI, and/or th e loss of your security clearances, whether intentional or inadvertent, may result in immediate termination. Before or during imposition of any discipline, employees will be given an opportunity to relate their version of the incident or problem at issue and provide any explanation or justification they consider relevant. Where appropriate, a policy of progressive employee redirection will be followed by supervisors. Major elements of this policy include: − Verbal Reprimand . The first step in NSI’s policy is the “verbal reprimand.” This is a verbal warning to an employee that his conduct is unacceptable, and that repeated or continued failure to conform his conduct or performance to NSI standards will result in more severe action. Before receiving a verbal reprimand, an employee will be counseled by his supervisor and told what improvements are necessary a nd expected to correct any performance deficiencies. A record of the notice of the verbal reprimand shall be made and retained in the employee's personnel file. − Written Reprimand . The second step is a “written reprimand.” This reprimand will describe the unacceptable conduct or performance of the employee and specify needed changes or improvements. A copy of the written reprimand will be retained in the empl oyee's personnel file. − Termination . The final step in the disciplinary procedure is the termination o f the employee. If an employee fails to modify his conduct or performance to conform to the standards required by NSI, the company may, in its sole discret ion, terminate the employee's employment. Notwithstanding this policy, NSI reserves the right to red irect employees in such a manner as it deems appropriate to the circumstances, and may, in its sole discretion, eliminate any or all of the steps in the discipline process. Policies and Procedures Page 14 of 74 www.NSIteam .com PPOOLLIICCYY NNOO.. 000044:: LLEEAAVVEE OOFF AABBSSEENNCCEE PPOOLLIICCIIEESS FFAAMMIILLYY AANNDD MMEEDDIICCAALL LLEEAAVVEE PPOOLLIICCYY NSI grants family and medical leaves of absence to “eligible employees” for the following: 1. Birth of an employee’s child or to care for the newborn child; 2. Placement of a child with the employee for adopti on or state- approved foster care; 3. Care of an employee’s spouse, child, or parent (“family member”) who has a serious health condition; or 4. Employee’s serious health condition which prevents the employee from performing any one essential function of the empl oyee’s position. A serious health condition is an illness, injury, impairment or physical or mental condition that involves either inpatient care or continuing treatment by a health care provider. Eligible Employee An active full -time or part -time employ ee is eligible for NSI Family and Medical Leave (NFML) in compliance with The Family and Medical Leave Act (FMLA) of 1993 (“ the Act”) provided that on the date the employee requests leave: 1. He/she has been actively employed by NSI full -time for at least 4 months; or 2. He/she has been actively employed by NSI part -time for at least 12 months. Length of Leave In accordance with th e FMLA, an eligible employee is entitled to a total of 12 workweeks of unpaid leave within a 12- month period. The amount of leave av ailable to an employee will be calculated by looking backward at the amount of leave taken within the 12 -month period immedi ately preceding the first date of leave. Leave taken for the care of a newborn child or placement for adoption or foster care must b e taken as an uninterrupted, continuous leave of absence and must be taken within 12 months of the birth or placement of the child. If both a husband and wife are employed by NSI and are eligible for leave, except for leave due to the employee’s serious health condition, the two may take a combined total of 12 -weeks. Intermittent leave or a reduced schedule may be approved for the employee’s serious health condition or a family member’s serious health condition where medically necessary and where the need for such leave is best accommodated through such scheduling. An employee requesting intermittent leave/reduced schedule may b e transferred temporarily to an available alternative position with equivalent pay and benefits, or to a part -time position if such a position better accommodates the need for intermittent leave/reduced schedule. NSI Family and Medical Leave Eligible employees are also entitled to 10 days of paid NSI Family and Medical Leave (NFML) on a 12 month rolling calendar to be used in the case of: 1. Birth of an employee’s child or to care for the newborn child; 2. Placement of a child with the employee for adoption or state -approved foster care; 3. Care of an employee’s spouse, child, or parent (“family member”) who has a serious health condition; 4. Employee’s serious health condition which prevents the employee from performing any one essential function of the employee’s po sition; or 5. Bereavement in the case of the death of an employee’s family member. A serious health condition is an illness, injury, impairment or physical or mental condition that involves either inpatient care or continuing treatment by a health care provi der. NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 15 of 74 www.NSIteam .com Substitution of Paid Leave An employee taking FMLA family and medical leave due to the employee’s serious health condition mus t substitute all accrued NFML family and medical leave before continuing leave on an unpaid basis. An employee taking leave for reasons other than an employee’s own serious health condition must exhaust all accrued NFML family and medical leave before cont inuing leave on an unpaid basis. Any family and medical leave, whether paid, unpaid, or a combination thereof, will be count ed toward the 12 -week leave entitlement. Employee Notification Requirements If an employee expects to take FMLA family and medical leave, the employee must notify their supervisor and NSI’s HR Coordinator of the intention to take leave at least 30 days in advance of the expected leave. Following proper notification, the employee must complete a Leave of Absence Request form and provid e any required medical certification. If the need for leave is not foreseeable, the employee must provide notification of l eave to their supervisor as soon as is practicable under the circumstances. An employee’s failure to provide 30 days advance notific ation for foreseeable leave may result in a delay of leave. Medical Certification An employee who takes leave for the emplo yee’s serious health condition or to care for a family member with a serious health condition must submit to NSI’s HR Coordinator written medical certification of the need for such leave from the applicable health care provider. Failure to provide the cert ification in a timely manner may result in a delay of leave. The health care provider may request a second or third medical opinion for verification of an employee’s serious health condition. The opinion of the third health care provider shall be final and binding on the employee. In addition, while the employee is on leave, the health care provider may require the employee to provide periodic recertification of the employee’s medical condition (not to exceed once every 30 days) and may inquire as to the em ployee’s intentions to return to work. An employee on uninterrupted, continuous leave due to the employee’s own serious health cond ition will be required to provide a job -related medical certification of fitness before the employee is allowed to return to work. Failure to provide this certification may result in the delay or denial of job restoration. Benefits Continuation The same h ealth care benefits coverage provided to an employee on the day prior to taking FMLA family and medical leave will be mainta ined during any NFML or vacation leave taken plus up to the 12- weeks or as required by law, provided the employee continues to pay a ny required contribution for benefits. Employees who are on leave are responsible for making their periodic payment of the r equired contribution. Upon completion of the FMLA family or medical leave, or if an employee fails to return to work at the end of the leave, a loss of coverage will occur, and continuation of health care coverage would be offered through COBRA. An employ ee who does not return from leave may be required, under certain circumstances provided by the Act, to reimburse NSI for any employee contributions paid by NSI while the employee was on unpaid leave. While on leave, an employee must continue to pay the em ployee’s contributions or loan payments for any applicable benefits which would otherwise be automatically deducted from the employee’s wages (e.g., supplemental lif e insurance, credit union loans and 401(k) loans). Contact NSI’s HR Coordinator and/or CPS for details regarding employee contributions and/or loan payments. The period of time an employee is on FMLA and/or NFML family and medical leave will be treated as continued service for purposes of vesting and eligibility to participate under any availab le pension or retirement plan. Absences due to leave will not be counted as time worked for the purpose of s eniority or computing va cation or sick/personal leave. Job Restoration NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 16 of 74 www.NSIteam .com An employee will be returned to the same or an equivalent position when the employee returns from FMLA and/or NFML family and medical leave, with no loss of benefits accrued prior to leave. An employee who does not return to work at the end of an authorized leave is subject to termination of employment. In the event an employee’s position with NSI is affected by a decision or event not related to the employee’s leave of absence, e.g., job elimination due to a reduction in force, the employee will be affected to the same extent as if he was not on leave. Certain “key employees ” as defined under The Family and Medical Leave Act of 1993 may not be eligible to be restored to the same or an equivalent position after leave if doing so would cause substantial and grievous economic injury to the operations of NSI . NSI will notify such employees of their “key employee” status and the conditions under which job restoration will be denied, if applicable. Workers' Compensation and Family and Medical Leave With some exceptions, an absence related to a workers' compensation injury is not counted against an employee's FMLA family and medical leave entitlement. If an employee who was injured on the job and as a result who suff ered a “ serious health condition ” declines the offer of a medically -approved “light duty ” position, the employee must notify NSI’s HR Coordinator that he chooses to exercise his FMLA family and medical leave rights, if he is so eligible. If the employee ac cepts the “light duty ” position in lieu of any FMLA family and medical leave or returns to work within 12 weeks after the da te of the injury, the employee will retain his right to be restored to the same or an equivalent position until 12 weeks have passed unless a decision or event not related to the employee's leave of absence occurs which results in the termination of the em ployee or the elimination of the job position. Questions about Family and Medical Leave If you have any questions about your rights or responsibilities under this policy, contact NSI’s HR Coordinator . NSI will comply with all applicable federal, state an d local laws in administering this policy. CCOONNTTIINNUUAATTIIOONN OOFF BBEENNEEFFIITTSS PPOOLLIICCYY It is the policy of NSI to provide the following health care benefits to employees who are away from work. An employee will be offered coverage through COBRA upon the expiration of 12 weeks in accordance with applicable law . Policies and Procedures Page 17 of 74 www.NSIteam .com Eligible employees may take up to 24 hours of leave during any 12- month per iod, in addition to leave available under FMLA, to participate in school activities directly related to the educational advancement of a son or daughter of the employee, such as parent -teacher conferences or interviewing for a new school; accompany the son or daughter of the employee to routine medical or dental appointments, such as check- ups or vaccinations; and accompany an elderly relative of the employee to routine medical or dental appointments or appointments for other professional services related t o the elder’s care, such as interviewing at nursing or group homes. GGEENNEERRAALL It is the responsibility of each employee to prepare, sign, and submit a timecard for each labor reporting period. It is a violation of NSI policy to willfully make a false statement or fraudulent representation through the completion of an individual time card. An employee willfully and consciously misrepresenting labor charges through the coding of time cards sha ll normally be subject to immediate suspension and likely dismissal by NSI . Attendance records are required for all employees, whether the employee is classified as exempt or non - exempt, and regardless of category (regular, temporary, or casual employee). The employee is responsible for accurate and complete attendance and labor reporting, and his/her supervisor is responsible for the verification. On 1 January 2009 NSI transition ed to a new automated, web -based timecard system Replicon . All timecard preparation, submission, and approval will take place using the web -based system. The manual procedures will be maintained for u se in the event that the web -based is not available or the employee cannot access the automated system. TTRRAAVVEELL EEXXPPEENNSSEE RREEPPOORRTT IINNFFOORRMMAATTIIOONN The following is an explanation of fields on the NSI Travel Expense Report (see below). − Name refers to the name of the employee traveling. − Origin refers to city where the trip began. This could mean city where you live or the office. − Destination refers your final destination, not the city where the airport is located. Your lodging p er diem will be based on this city. − Departure Time refers to the time when your travel began, for example, either from your home or the office. It does not mean the time of your flight. − Return Time refers to the time when yo ur travel ended. This means time when you arrived home or to the office or other place of business. It does not mean the time of your flight. − Reason for Travel should be detailed enough to allow an auditor to clearly understand the intended purpose of the trip. If you are conducting busi ness development, state it such that an auditor would know and with whom the business development efforts were conducted. − Lodging Pe r Diem – Employees will be reimbursed based on the government approved per diem rates for the destination city. Please go to the official per diem website. − NOTE : Meal and Incidental per diem rates are listed separately on the website and should be combined on the “M&IE Per Diem” line on the Travel Expense Report form. If needing to adjust the “M&IE” amounts for meals covered by NSI, please refer to the GSA per diem site http://www.gsa.gov/portal/catego ry/21287 . A general rule of thumb is: breakfast, 15%; lunch, 25%; dinner, 50%; incidentals, 5%. If the employee’s actual ho tel rate is higher than the per diem rate, the employee will only be reimbursed for the excess amount if approved by NSI’s CE O. If not approved, the employee will be reimbursed at the government per diem rate and, in addition, the hotel tax will be reduced to the amount that would have been charged at per diem. The following website provides a link to hotels that charge the government per diem rate: http://www.hotelsatperdiem.com . When making your room reserva tion, please confirm that the rate to be charged by the hotel matches the lodging per diem rate. PPEERRSSOONNAALL TTIIMMEE WWHHIILLEE OONN NNSSII TTRRAAVVEELL If an employee goes on a business trip but extend s the visit for personal reasons, in addition to the receipt for the actual airfare, the employee must provide a printout of the airfare and itinerary for the times of travel that would have applied had he not extended his travel. The printout needs to be attached to the expense report along with the actual airfare receipt. The e mployee will be reimbursed for the lesser of what the airfare would have been or the actual airfare. PPUURRPPOOSSEE The purpose of this policy is to document the policy for the NSI Career Advancement Path . The NSI Career Advancement Path requires demonstrated excellence in three main areas in order to for an individual to be conside red for promotion. The three fundamental areas that are critical for each individual on the technical side of the company to show co mpetence, expertise and experience are: Technical, Management, and Business Development. BB.. SSCCOOPPEE The scope of the policy incl udes: 1. The technical advancement path, which consists of two parallel paths, one for analysts, and one for scientists. 2. Requirements for eligibility for promotion. 3. Key factors that will be considered for promotions. CC.. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy i s outlined below . DD.. GGEENNEERRAALL The NSI Technical Advancement Path will contain two parallel paths. As NSI is a young, small company this focus on the technical career path is sufficient, however an analogous management track will be developed as necessary. The following is the technical advancement path: The “Analyst Path” consists of the following positions: Member of Technical Staff, An alyst, Senior Analyst, Principal Analyst, Director and Chief Analyst. The “Scientist Path” consists of the following positi ons: Member of Technical Staff, Scientist, Senior Scientist, Principal Scientist, Director and Chief Scientist. Eligibility for Pro motion: The three fundamental areas where competence, expertise and experience must be shown to be considered for promotions are Technical, Management, and Business Development. Technical competence, expertise and experience are demonstrated through forma l training in undergraduate programs, graduate programs, continuing education, through contributions in NSI project related work, publications in the field of formal training, and through teaching. Management competence, expertise and experience are demon strated in project, personnel and other corporate management functions . In general, management functions include clearly defining, setting and ensuring successful execution of goals, objectives, deliverables, and overall scope of the task and/or project. Additiona lly, it requires establishing staffs plan to execute the task and/or project , identifying the activities needed to c omplete the deliverables in a timely manner, on budget . Project managers are responsible for budget and schedule plans , which includ e estimating time and cost for activities as well as risk planning. Monitoring and controls must be set in place by the project manager to allow for measurement of the ongoing project activities, project variables, and making adjustments in execution as ne cessary. Business Development competence, expertise and experience are demonstrated in a variety of ways, including develop ing winning proposals, assessing marketing opportunities and target markets for NSI and its services, and relationship building with clients and potential clients. Additionally, experience should include: generating leads for possible sales, including foll ow-up sales activity; attending briefings and presentations and preparing materials that sell NSI’s messag e; and participating in pi tch and proposition development. Key Factors for Promotion: NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 29 of 74 www.NSIteam .com In order to be promoted along a given technical path the key fa ctors that will be considered for promotions include the amount of formal training an individual has and the years and type of exper ience they have gained. Additionally, key factors include the level of competence, expertise and experience one has gained and demonstrated throughout one’s career as well as within NSI. In order to be eligible for a promotion , sustained competence, expertise and experience consistent with the table below is required . Sub accounts will be as signed a letter under the general account number. The grouping of the accounts into the series provides a method of accumulating and accounting for costs for financial and cost accounting purposes. − Current Assets 1000 Series Current Assets are cash or o ther resources commonly identified as those, which are reasonably expected to be realized in cash or sold or consumed during the nor mal operating cycle of the business. Current assets may include Cash, Marketable Securities, Receivables and Inventories. − Fixed Assets 1100 Series Fixed Assets are Property, Plant and Equipment used by the business entity to generate revenue and profits . Fixed Assets may include Land, Buildings and Machinery and Equipment − Other Assets 1200 Series Other Assets are intangib le assets, prepayments and assets that could not be classified as Curren t or Fixed. Other Assets may include Patents, Copyrights, Li censes, Prepaid Insurances, etc. − Current Liabilities 2000 Series NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 33 of 74 www.NSIteam .com Current Liabilities are obligations whose liquidation is expected to require the use of existing resources within the operating cycle of the business entity. Current Liabilities include Tr ade Accounts Payable, Payroll Tax Payables, Interest Payable, etc. − Long -Term Liabilities 2100 Series Long-Term Liabilities are all obligations not meeting the criteria for Current Liabilities. Long-Term Liabilities are long -term notes, bonds, mortgages o r customer advances. − Other Liabilities 2200 Series Other Liabilities are liabilities that could not be classified as curr ent or long -term. − Stockholder’s Equity 3000 Series Stockholder’s Equity r epresents the stockhol der’s interest in the c ompany. Equity accounts include Common Stock, Preferred Stock, Paid -In Capital and Retained Earnings. − Contract Revenue 4000 Series Contract Revenue r epresents revenue generated by contracts with Government Agencies and Commercial entities. − Cost of Goods Sold 5000 Series Costs directly related to specific final cost objectives or contracts of NSI. Indirect Cost – Any cost not directly identified with a single, final cost objective, but identified with two or more final cost object ives or an intermediate cost objective. Final Cost Objective – A cost objective that has allocated to it both direct and in direct costs and is the final accumulation point for the cost accounting system . DDEEFFIINNIITTIIOONNSS Unallowable Cost – Any cos t which, under the provisions of any pertinent, law, regulation, or contract, cannot be included in prices, cost -reimburseme nts, or settlements under a Government contract to which it is allocable . Expressly Unallowable Cost – A particular item or type of cost which, under the express provisions of an applicable law, regulation, or contract, is specifically named and stated to be unallowable . Directly Associated Cost – Any cost which is generated solely as a result of the incurrence of another cost, and w hich would not have been incurred had the cost not been incurred . The first voucher on a contract is effectively an interim voucher, as are all subsequent vouchers pri or to the final or completion voucher. A final “completion ” voucher will not be submitted until all contract work is complet ed. Any intentional misrepresentation of incurred costs may constitute fraud and result in fines, imprisonment, or debarment from Go vernment contracting . SSCCOOPPEE 1. PPRREEPPAARRIINNGG TTHHEE BBIILLLLSS Cost Plus Fixed Fee (CPF F) Contracts NSI must use SF 1034 (original) and 1034A (copies), “Public Voucher for Purchases and Services Other Than Perso nal,” to show the amount claimed for reimbursement. Firm Fixed Price (FFP) Contracts – Performance or Milestone Billings Performance- based payments are not based on costs, but on events or other quant ifiable measures of results. There is no specified format or Standard Form for the paper submission of performance- based pay ments. However, electronic submission of performance- based payments can be made thr ough Wide Area Workflow (WAWF). NSI must maintai n records and controls to adequately administer performance- based payments. This includes furnishing reports, certificates, financial statements, and other pertinent information requested by the NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 42 of 74 www.NSIteam .com contracting officer to either administer the payment or to determine that an event or other criterion has been successfully accomplished. Firm Fixed Price (FFP) Contracts – Progress P ayments Progress payments are a form of Government furnished interest -free financing applicable to undelivered and un-invoiced items . Progress payments shall be made to NSI when requested as work progresses, not more frequently than monthly, in amounts approved by the contracting officer. Unless a request is made for a smaller amount, each progress payment shall be computed at the rate stipulated in the progress payment clause of the contract, using the total costs under the contract as shown by the account ing books and records. NSI may add to this amount progress payments made to subcontractors or other company divisions. The progress payment request must also be adjusted for the sum of previous progress payments. Contracts awarded to small business concern s are handled in a similar fashion, but the rate of recovery is normally high er. Cost-based progress payments are requested on a SF 1443 progress payment request form. The contract will designate an address to which these forms are submitted (the billing address) and the distribution, number of copies, etc Time and Material (T&M) Contracts Time and Material billings will be prepared and submitted in accordance with the terms o f the contract or subcontract. The bonus plan is to financially reward employees who deliver superior technical, fiscal, and/or managerial results. Individual eligible employees will participate in bonus awards commensurate with their relative job performance . SSCCOOPPEE 1. NSI bonus plan policy and eligibility. 2. NSI bonus evaluation criteria. 3. NSI bonus plan procedure. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy is outlined below . PPOOLLIICCYY NSI’s Board of Directors (BOD) will establish an annual bonus pool for the purpose of setting aside overhead monies for bonuses. NSI will fund this annual bonus pool based upon the degree of NSI’s achievement of its designated Fiscal Objectives for the ye ar. AAPPPPLLIICCAABBIILLIITTYY,, MMOODDIIFFIICCAATTIIOONN//TTEERRMMIINNAATTIIOONN,, && LLIIMMIITTAATTIIOONNSS All NSI employees on the payroll at the time bonuses are approved by the BOD will be eligible to participate in the bonus plan. Employees who have worked a partial year will have their bonus potential pro -rated based on the amount of time worked at NSI. The extent to which bonuses are accrued is at the sole discretion of the BOD and the amount of funding released to pay -out bonus awards is the function of how well NSI meets its designated Fiscal Objectives as well as NSI employees achieving their individual objectives . Bonuses are not guaranteed entitlements and NSI may decide to rescind, retract, modify, amend, or terminate this policy, in whole or in part at any time, for any reason whatsoever b y majority vote of its BOD . DDEEFFIINNIITTIIOONNSS Annual Bonus Plan The Annual Bonus Plan is an employee incentive program designed to advanc e the interests of both the employer and employee by making the achievement of certain objectives and delivery of superior q uality performance reciprocally beneficial to both. The Bonus Plan year is the calendar year that is also NSI’s fiscal year. Bonus Accrual Rate A bonus accrual rate is selected each year for purposes of establishing the annual Overhead budget. It is stated in terms of percentage of payroll. The BOD sets this accrual rate when they accept the annual budget. The chief reason for predetermining an accrual rate is to make sure adequate funds are set aside on an accrual basis to actually pay out bonus. This acc rual rate is set for budgetary purposes and Executive Management may revise it with the BOD’s approval during the year, if circumsta nces warrant such revision. An accrual rate is typically set, or revised, based on existing or predicted economic conditions for the year. For example, Executive Management may adjust the accrual rate upward if it believes there is a strong likelihood that NSI will materially exceed its Fiscal Objectives . Operational Fiscal Objectives Fiscal Objectives are annual goals develop ed by Executive M anagement and accepted by the BOD . The Fiscal Objectives may vary from year to year based on the tactical and strat egic needs of NSI . The meeting of these NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 44 of 74 www.NSIteam .com goals typically has a direct bearing on NSI ’s ability to fund the bonus pool. Execut ive Management may revise Fiscal Objectives with the BOD’s approval during the year, if circumstances warrant such revision. Total Funded Bonus Pool This amount is computed based on the 1) Bonus Accrual Amount and 2) percent achievement of specified fiscal goals. This amount represents the maximum potential amount of bonus dollars that could be given out in any given year under the pl an. Bonus Awards to Employees Eligible employees who participate in bonus awards are those who have delivered performance that meets or exceeds the normal expectations and requirements for their positions, thereby resulting in the delivery of superior tec hnical, fiscal, and/or managerial quality. No bonus awards will be made to persons not meeting the expectations of their pos ition. All employees who meet the expectation s of their job position s are eligible to receive a bonus, though it is expected that th e majority of the bonus pool will be distributed to those persons exceeding the expectations and requirements for their posi tions. Performance evaluations will be conducted in accordance with NSI’s Performance Review Policy. For each employee, Executive Ma nagement shall review and concur with their overall performance rating before it is given to the employee. Overall Rating D efinition Exceptional: Employee always gets results far beyond what is required. Exceeds Requirements : Employee goes above and beyo nd expectations. Meets Requirements: Employee meets basic requirements. Tasks are completed on time. Marginal: Employee needs improvement in quality of work. Completes tasks, but not on time. Unsatisfactory: Employee d oes not perform required tasks. Req uires constant supervision . PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE General In December, Executive Management will set fiscal and/or operational goals f or the next fiscal year. Likewise, in December, or at the start of an employee’s employment, certain goals will be set that are coup led to corporate goals. Additionally, employees will be expected to perform at, or above, professional expectations in the position for which they were hired. Adoption of Bonus and Fiscal Objectives NSI’s Bonus and Fiscal Objectives will be set forth in t he Annual Budget prepared for the Board of Directors’ review and approval. Fiscal objectives will be disclosed to employees by their Manager. Each employee will have their annual objectives communicated to them in December by their Manager. Determination of Pool Funding After November is closed, Executive M anagement will calculate the expected amount of bonus dollars for the next fiscal year based on the projected year’s payroll and the expected percentage achievement of fiscal goals. This calculation will determine the bonus pool amount for the year . Determination of Participation All managers will complete “draft” Performanc e Reviews for their employees in accordance with NSI ’s Performance Review process , no later than December 1 of the year. The Perform ance Review will include an assessment of achievement of any specific annual objectives set for them. The Draft reviews will be forwarded by Managers to Executive Management for review. After their review, Executive Management will provide feedback by the end of the second week of December . Final Performance Reviews will be completed by the end of the third week of December . These Final Reviews will be the basis for distribution of the bonus pool. Payment Bonuses will be become payable as soon as practicab le upon their determination. For regular staff, bonuses will generally be paid out in December, but may be paid out later if warranted by unforeseen financial NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 45 of 74 www.NSIteam .com anomalies. For executive officers, a portion of bonuses may be paid out in December at the time o f regular staff bonuses, but a portion may be withheld until final determination of company performance. Inappropriate use of NSI ’s resource s could expose NSI , its employees, its customers and other third parties to risks, including virus attacks, compromise of network systems and services, damages, and other legal issues . SSCCOOPPEE NSI acceptable use policy of computer and information technology . PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy is outlined below . PPOOLLIICCYY NSI’s intention for publishing this policy is not to i mpose restrictions that are contrary to our culture of openness, trust and integrity. Notwithstanding, NSI is committed to protectin g itself, its employees, and third parties from illegal or damaging actions committed by individuals using NSI resources, ei ther knowingly or unknowingly. Internet/intranet/extranet -related systems, including but not limited to computer equipment, softwar e, operating systems, storage media, network accounts providing electronic mail, World Wide Web (“WWW”) browsing, and file t ransfer protocol (“FTP ”), are the property of NSI . These systems are to be used for business purposes in serving the interests of the company, and of our clients and customers in the course of normal operations. PCs and email services may be used for incid ental non -commercial personal use, as long as such use does not violate the standards of acceptable use set forth in this policy or provisions of any other NSI policy. NSI use of equipment, server space and computing services will always be given priority over personal use. Effective security is a team effort involving the participation and support of every NSI employee and affiliate who deals with information and/or information systems. It is the responsibility of every computer user to know these guideli nes, and to conduct their activities accordingly. AAPPPPLLIICCAABBIILLIITTYY This policy applies to all equipment that is owned or leased by NSI. This policy applies to all employees, and to all contractors, consultants, temporary employees, and other workers at NSI , including all personnel affiliated with third parties, using NSI ’s equipment. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE General Use and Ownership − While NSI desires to provide a reasonable level of privacy, users should be aware that the data they create on the corporate systems remains the property of NSI. Because of the need to protect and monitor NSI’s electronic business assets/operations and its duty to comply w ith various federal, state, and local laws, Management cannot and does not guarantee the privacy or confidentiality of infor mation stored on any device belonging to NSI . − Employees are responsible for exercising good judgment regarding the reasonableness of personal use and if there is any uncertainty, employees should consult their supervisor or NSI’s Information Systems Manage r. − For security and network maintenance purposes, authorized individuals within NSI may monitor equipment, systems and network traffic, and electronic files at any time. NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 47 of 74 www.NSIteam .com − NSI reserves the right to audit network and systems to ensure compliance with this pol icy. NSI reserves the right to engage in monitoring of electronic mail messages or other electronic files created by employees using NSI resources. Monitoring may include, but is not limited to, the type, volume, frequency, work relatedness, and size of el ectronic files and email traffic. Security and Proprietary Information − Employees should take all necessary steps to prevent unautho rized access to NSI Proprietary Information (e.g., passwords, payroll records, proposals, bid rates, project files, access t o intranet, etc.). − Absolutely no viewing, storing, processing or sharing of classified data is authorized on any of NSI ’s computer s ystems except for single stand -alone systems in the care and custody of NSI Information Systems Manager. − Keep passwords secu re and do not share accounts. Authorized users are responsible for the security of their passwords and accounts. Guest log -on(s) for authorized NSI visitors are available and may be obtained by contacting the Information Systems Manager. − All PCs, laptops a nd workstations should be secured with a password -protected screensaver with an automatic activation feature set to go on when left unattended for any time greater than 15 minutes. − Postings by employees from an NSI email address to newsgroups or other onli ne forums should contain a disclaimer stating that the opinions expressed are strictly their own and not those of NSI , unless postin g is in the course of authorized business duties. It is further required to follow this procedure when sending personal emai ls. ”The views expressed in this email message are the personal opinions of the author and do not represent those of the company pro viding email services.” − All hosts used by the employee that are connected to the NSI internet/intranet/extranet, whether owned by the employee or NSI , shall use real-time virus -protection software. − Employees must use extreme caution when opening email atta chments received from unknown senders, which may contain malicious code (e.g., viruses, email bombs, or Trojan horse code). Unacceptable Use − The follo wing activities are prohibited. Under no circumstances is an employee of NSI authorized to engage in any activity that is illegal under any local, state, federal or international law or any contract provision while utilizing NSI-owned resources. The lists below are by no means exhaustive, but attempt to provide a framework for activities that fall into the ca tegory of unacceptable use. − Violations of the rights of any person or company protected by copyright, trade secret, patent o r other intellectual property, or similar laws or regulations, including, but not limited to, the installation or distribution of “ pirated ” or other software products that are not appropriately licensed for use by NSI . − Unauthorized copying of copyrighted m aterial including, but not limited to, digitization and distribution of photographs from magazines, books or other copyrighted sourc es, copyrighted music, and the installation of any copyrighted software for which NSI does not have an active license is str ictly prohibited. − Exporting software, technical information, encryption software or technology, in violation of international or reg ional export control laws, is illegal. The appropriate management should be consulted prior to export of any material that i s in question. − Introduction of malicious programs into the network or server (e.g., viruses, worms, Trojan horses, email bombs, etc. ). − Revealing your account password to others or allowing use of your account by others. This includes family and ot her house hold members when working at home. − Using an NSI computing asset to actively engage in procuring or transmitting material that is in violation of sexual harassment or hostile workplace laws. − Using an NSI computer to produce, sell, trade, transfer, or access any type of pornographic material whatsoever. − Making fraudulent offers of products, items, or services originating from an NSI account. − Making statements about warranty, expressly or implied, unless it is a part of normal job duties. − Effecting security b reaches or disruptions of network communication. Security breaches include, but are not limited to, accessing data of which the empl oyee is not an intended recipient or logging into a server or account that the employee is not expressly authorized to acces s, unless these duties are within the NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 48 of 74 www.NSIteam .com scope of regular duties. For purposes of this section, “ disruption ” includes, but is not limit ed to, network sniffing, ping floods, packet spoofing, denial of service, and forged routing information for malicious purpo ses. − Port scanning or security scanning is expressly prohibited unless prior approval of NSI’s Information Systems Manager is made. − Executing any form of network monitoring which will intercept data not intended for the employee's host, unless this activit y is a part of the employee's normal job/duty. − Circumventing user authentication or security of any host, network or account. − Interfering with or denying service to any user other than the employee's host (for example, denial of service attack). − Using any program/script/command, or sending messages of any kind, with the intent to interfere with, or disable, a user's terminal, via any m eans, locally or via the Internet/intranet/extranet. − Sending unsolicited email messages, including the sending of “junk mail ” or other advertising material to individuals who did not specifica lly request such material . − Any form of harassment via email, tel ephone or paging, whether through language, frequency, or size of messages. − Unauthorized use, or forging, of email header in formation. − Solicitation of email for any other email address, other than that of the poster's account, with the intent to harass or to collect replies. − Creating or forwarding “ chain letters ” or other “ pyramid ” schemes of any type. − Posting the same or simil ar non -business -related messages to large numbers of Usenet newsgroups (newsgroup spam) EENNFFOORRCCEEMMEENNTT Any employee found to have viol ated this policy could be subject to disciplinary action, up to and including termination of employment.
