Policies and Procedures Page 49 of 74 www.NSIteam .com PPOOLLIICCYY NNOO.. 001166:: PPAAIIDD OOVVEERRTTIIMMEE AANNDD EEXXTTEENNDDEEDD HHOOUURRSS PPUURRPPOOSSEE The purpose of this policy is to document the policy for the conditions under which pai d overtime and extended hours will be authorized and how it will be managed by NSI. SSCCOOPPEE NSI paid overtime and extended hours policy. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy is outlined below . GGEENNEERRAALL PPOOLLIICCYY AANNDD PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE All employees will be paid onc e per month on the last work day of the month. For paydays falling on a Saturday or holiday, you will be paid the prior business day. For paydays falling on a Sunday, you will be paid the following business day. NSI highly encourages all employees to use d irect deposit of their checks. If you are absent on payday and someone else is to pick up your check, it will not be released without a s igned, handwritten note from you authorizing the named person to pick it up. The person designated to pick up your check will be asked to produce identification satisfactory to management; otherwise, your check will not be released. Any deviations from thi s procedure must have prior approval from the NSI CE O. It is NSI's standard policy to expect all professional (exempt) employees to complete their assignments working no more than 40 hours per week. Notwithstanding, NSI recognizes that occasional situatio ns arise that require professional staff to work extended hours (more than 40 hours per week). Paid overtime (exceeding 40 hours per week) for salaried employees, at a straight hourly rate, will be used only in the event of special staffing requirements th at cannot be satisfied by any other reasonable means. Such additional pay, where approved by the employee supervisor an d NSI C EO, will be at an amount equivalent to 1/40th of the employee’s regular weekly salary for each extra hour worked. Vacation, sick/personal and holiday pay will be paid on the regular pay cycle. If you resign, final settlement of services or wages wi ll be made no earlier than the next regular pay cycle, or in accordance with state law, whichever is sooner. If you are terminated, you w ill be issued a check on the next regular payday, or in accordance with applicable state law, whichever is earlier. Payout of vacation will be limited to 160 hours. There will be no payout for sick/personal leave. AAPPPPLLIICCAABBIILLIITTYY This po licy applies to all employees; however an individual's treatment under this policy is dependent upon their employment status (exempt vs. n on-exempt). Exempt employees are typically salaried or part -time hourly professionals that have a large degree of freedom in deciding how to accomplish their work tasks. They are referred to as 'exempt' because certain labor laws, that guarantee such thing s as overt ime pay, do not apply to them. Non -exempt personnel are typically employees that work on an hourly basis in non - professional po sitions where they exercise a limited amount of discretion. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE It should be recognized that overtime and additi onal work other than that which is regularly scheduled might be required. Overtime will be paid to eligible, non -exempt employees in acco rdance with applicable state law. The pay for regular overtime will be at the federal or state prescribed wage rate, wh ichever is higher. All overtime must be authorized prior to its occurrence by your immediate supervisor and the NSI CE O. All overtime wi ll be clearly noted on your time sheet and should be initialed by your immediate supervisor. Managers that supervise no n-exempt employees may authorize overtime to the extent that the associated NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 50 of 74 www.NSIteam .com costs do not exceed their budget. Overtime must be authorized in advance by the NSI C EO and the authorizing manager who is then responsible for ensuring that the overtime is utiliz ed efficiently and effectively. Non-Exempt Employee Overtime Managers that supervise non- exempt employees may authorize overtime to the extent that the associated costs do not exceed their budget. Overtime must be authorized in advance and the authorizing manager is responsible for ensuring that the overtime is utilized efficiently and effectively. NSI will pay pre -authorized overtime to non -exempt hourly employees at the rate of 150% for all time worked in excess of 40 hours in a one week pay period. Exempt Employee Overtime The NSI CE O will consider authorizing extended hours (extra pay for exempt personnel) under the following circumst ances: − There are pending staffing requirements that cannot be effectively met by: o moving personnel between assignments ; o requesting contract extensions; or o the use of contract personnel. − The staffing dilemma cannot be resolved by staff increases either bec ause: o the need is too short -term in nature to make hiring a prudent decision, or o the required talent is not readily ava ilable in the labor market. The NSI CE O will review the work backlog on all ongoing contracts and determine which jobs, if any, should be candidates for extended hours. If a decision is made to evoke extended hours under any contract, employees will be in formed in writing by an “Extended Hours Notice” that specifies the anticipated period of extended hours and the contracts affected. This notice, by itself, does not authorize additional pay, but rather, informs employees that NSI is in extended hour’s mode on specific contracts. Additional pay for extra hours worked by an exempt employee must also be verbally authorized by the Project Mana ger prior to being worked. After the Extended Hours Notice is given, the Project Manager should coordinate additional h ours worked with individual project personnel. The following items should be mutually agreed to during the authorization discussion betwe en the Project Manager and the employee: − The number of hours the employee is expected to work during the extended hour s period (or shorter period, such as the next week, if more appropriate). − The technical objectives the employee will direct his efforts t owards during such additional hours. − A general agreement on the time (i.e. week- ends, nights) and place (i.e. home, off ice) where the additional hours will be worked. − If an employee feels that additional time is needed to accomplish certain technical objec tives, he must secure the Project Manager's verbal approval prior to expending the additional time. All professional ( exempt) staff working extended hours will be paid at a rate equivalent to 1/40th of their weekly salary for the number of hours worked in excess of the calendar month's normal billable hours (calculated by multiplying the number of week days in the calenda r month by 8). SSCCOOPPEE NSI paid leave policy. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy is outlined below . PPOOLLIICCYY NSI’s emplo yee benefits package includes paid holiday, sick/personal, and vacation leave for all eligible emplo yees. AAPPPPLLIICCAABBIILLIITTYY All NSI employe es scheduled to work at least 50% time (approximately 20 hours per week) will be granted paid leave for vacation, sic k/personal time, and holidays. Except for negotiated agreements with key personnel, eligible employees will earn paid leave in accordance w ith the terms of this policy as set forth below. DDEEFFIINNIITTIIOONNSS Vacation - Vacation time is leave taken at an employee’s discretion with at least one week’s advance notice to his/her supervisor. Regular full -time employees are eligible for paid vacation time during each calendar year. A paid vacation does not count as a day worked in calculating overtime. Sick/Personal Time - Sick/personal time is leave taken by the employee for personal or family health reasons, including, but not limited to: doctors or den tists appointments, death in the family, need for a household repair person, etc. Except in cases of dire emergency, no tice of such leave should be given as far in advance as possible to the employee’s supervisor. Regular full -time employees are eligible for paid sick/personal time during each calendar year. Paid sick/personal time does not count as a day worked in calcula ting overtime. Holiday Time - Holiday time is leave taken for traditional national holidays as designated by NSI or for religious/person al holidays taken at the employee’s discretion with at least one week’s advance notice to his/her supervisor. Regular f ull-time employees are eligible for paid holidays during each calendar year. A paid holiday does not count as a day worked in calculating overtime. NSI observes the following holidays each year: 1. New Year's Day 2. Birthday of Martin Luther King, Jr. 3. Washingto n's Birthday 4. Memorial Day 5. Independence Day 6. Labor Day 7. Columbus Day 8. Veterans Day 9. Thanksgiving Day 10. Christmas Day NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 52 of 74 www.NSIteam .com PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE General Paid lea ve is a benefit that is earned on a prorated basis over each monthly period. Vacation Leave Eligible NSI employees wil l earn paid vacation leave as set forth in the table below. Position Monthly Accrual Annual Vacation Leave Scientist/Analyst 6.67 hours 2 weeks Senior Level Employee 10 hours 3 weeks Principals and Above 13.33 hours 4 weeks Each regular, full -time em ployee will earn no less than 10 days (8 0 hours) of vacation upon the completion of one year of employment with NSI. Due to seniority, so me employees are hired into NSI eligible to earn 15 days ( 120 hours) or 20 days ( 160 hours) of vacation upon the comple tion of one year of employment with NSI. Whether an employee is eligible for 10 days (80 hours) or 15 days ( 120 hours) of vacation, upon the completion of three years of employment, employees will earn an additional 5 days (40 hours) of vacation. The maxim um amount of vacation an employee is eligible for is 20 days ( 160 hours) . Vacation hours do roll over from one calendar year to the next , with a maximum balance of 80 hours. Any vacation hours above the 80 hour maximum that are not used by the end of the calendar year will be lost. If you leave NSI, you will be paid for accrued but unused vacation up to 160 hours maximum computed at the r ate of pay earned upon separation provided you give two weeks written notice and are not being terminated for misconduc t. Employees should give as much notice as possible in scheduling vacation time. If there are conflicting dates, preference will be giv en to the employee who has the most seniority. A more junior employee who already has an approved vacation date will no t, however, be bumped by a more senior employee. Employees who are away from work on a leave of absence do not accrue vacation time whil e on leave. Sick/Personal Leave Eligible NSI employees will earn paid sick/personal leave as set forth below. Yrs of Employment Monthly Accrual Annual Sick/Personal Leave All years 8 hours 12 days NSI recognizes that inability to work because of illness or injury may cause economic hardship. For this reason, NSI provides paid sick/personal days to full -time regular em ployees. Eligible employees accrue sick/personal days at the rate of 1 day (8 hours) per month up to a maximum of 12 days (96 hours) per calendar year. Unused sick/personal time does not roll over from one calendar year to the next . No payments will be made for accrued but unused sick/personal time at the end of any calendar year or in the event of termination . In special need circumstan ces as identified by NSI, employees may contribute up to 1/3 of their own accrued sick/personal time to another employee’s sick/personal time pool. Leave for illness or injury in excess of five consecutive working days, or more than ten days in any one thirty-day period, must be supported by a written physician’s statement supporting the medical necessity of the leave. NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 53 of 74 www.NSIteam .com Holiday Leave Eligible NSI employees will earn paid holiday leave as set forth below. Yrs of Employment Monthly Accrual Annual Holiday Le ave All years 6.67 hours 2 weeks These holidays are “floating” which means they can be taken at any point during the calendar year; however, they do not roll over from one calendar year to the next, which means any unused holiday hours not used by the e nd of the calendar year will be lost. Holiday leave may not be accrued; it must be taken in the calendar year earned o r it will be forfeited. N o payments will be made for accrued but unused holiday leave in the event of termination. SSCCOOPPEE The “NSI Scholarship” is intended to encourage eligible NSI employees to pursue further education beneficial both to the employee and to NSI. The NSI Scholarship is designed to be non -taxable to the employee up to the limits specified under the then current IRS Code Section 127(a). PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedures for the NSI Scholarship Assistance Program are outlined belo w. Eligibility Active, full -time employees who own less than 5% of the Company are eligible for the non -income taxable NSI Scholarship. Employees who own 5% or more of the Company are eligible for the NSI Scholarship as added taxable income. Coverage The NSI Scholarship can be applied to any NSI -approved course of study at an accredited institution. The NSI Scholarship will be paid in the form of a reimbursement for expenses incurred by the student provided the student : 1. successfully completes the course with a grade of C or higher ; 2. submits reimbursement claim s comprised of a transcript and proof of payment no later than 45 days following the end of the course. Eligible employees enrolled in approved non -degree programs (e.g., college courses outside a d egree program, professional certification, certificate programs, continuing education, etc.) may receive up to a $2000 “NSI Scholarship” award per calendar year . Eligible employees enrolled in approved undergraduate or graduate degree programs may receive up to a $ 6000 “NSI Scholarship” award per calendar year . Eligible employees must obtain written approval from his/her manager and the NSI C EO prior to starting a course for which an NSI Scholarship award is being sought . NSI Scholarship awards will be paid in the form of a reimbursement upon course completion for course-related tuition, fees, books, materials, etc . There is no roll-over of unused scholarship funds into subsequent years. Ineligible Expenses The following expenses and fees are not covered b y the NSI Scholarship Assistance Program : • Expenses covered by a fellowship, grant, scholarship or other financial aid • Membership or licensing fees or dues • Parking/transportation, meals, lodging expenses • General use, postage, late fees or finance charges • Transcript, graduation fees or any other fee not directly associated with coursework Filing a Claim NSI Scholarsh ip moni es are reimbursements – the employee must submit paperwork (i .e., transcripts , documentation of eligible payment, proof of payment and a course overview ) to NSI’s HR Coordinator . PPOOLLIICCYY Federal agencies maintain hotlines to provide an unconstrained avenue for government and contractor employees to report, without fear of reprisal, known or suspected instances of serious security irregularities and infr actions concerning contracts, programs, or projects. These hotlines do not supplant contractor responsibility to facilitate reporting and timely investigation of security matters concerning its operations or personnel, and contractor personnel are encourag ed to furnish information through established company channels. However, the hotline may be used as an alternate means to report this type of information when considered prudent or necessary. Policies and Procedures Page 56 of 74 www.NSIteam .com PPOOLLIICCYY NNOO.. 002200:: TTEECCHHNNOOLLOOGGYY CCOONNTTRROOLL PPLLAANN ((TTCCPP)) PPUURRPPOOSSEE The purpose of thi s Technology Control Plan ( TCP) is to delineate and inform employees of National Security Innovations (NSI) of the cont rols necessary to ensure that no transfer of technical information or data or a defense service, as defined and protected in ITAR paragra phs 120.10 & 120.9, occurs unless authorized by the Office of Defense Trade Controls (ODTC) of Department of State (DoS ). SSCCOOPPEE The policy and procedures contained in this plan apply to all divisions of NSI . Disclosure of unclassified technical data and/o r information, as defined and protected under ITAR, to foreign persons in a visitor status or in the course of their em ployment by NSI is considered an export disclosure under the International Traffic in Arms Regulations (ITAR) and requires a DoS license or DoS approval of either a Technical Assistance Agreement or a Manufacturing License Agreement . BBAACCKKGGRROOUUNNDD NSI is a s mall, privately -owned business that specializes in providing innovative and pragmatic scientific, technical, analytical and programmatic services and solutions to a broad range of 21st century national security problems. NSI brings unique expertise and ext ensive experience in developing, integrating and applying quantitative and computational modeling and analysis technology rooted in the principles from social, physical and information science for problems in counter -terrorism, foreign intelligence, stabil ity analysis, deterrence operations, socio -cultural human terrain mapping, strategic assessment and ot her national security matters. NSI is an IT-enabled , network- centric virtual organization with staff in several states . UU..SS.. PPEERRSSOONN//FFOORREEIIGGNN PPEERRSSOONN The In ternational Trade and Arms Regulations (ITAR) define a U.S. person and a foreign person as follows . − A U.S. person means a U.S. citizen or a person who is a lawful permanent resident ( has a green card). It also means any corporation, business association, p artnership, society, trust or any other entity, organization or group that is incorporated to do business in the United States. It also i ncludes any governmental federal, state or local entity. A person or employee with an H -1 visa status is not a U.S. per son. − A foreign person means a person who is not a lawful permanent resident. It also means any, foreign corporation, business association , partnership, trust, society or any other entity or group that is not incorporated or organized to do business in the United States, as well as international organizations, foreign governments and any agency or subdivision of foreign governments (e.g., di plomatic missions). AACCCCEESSSS CCOONNTTRROOLL FFOORR FFOORREEIIGGNN NNAATTIIOONNAALLSS Foreign Person Restrictions Foreign person restrictions apply as follows: 1. No foreign person will be given access to classified or unclassified export controlled material on any project or program u ntil that individual's license authority has been approved by ODTC. 2. NSI employees who have supervisory responsibilities for foreign persons will receive an export control/licensing briefing that addresses relevant ITAR requirements as they pertain to expor t controlled information. 3. No foreign national will have access to any cleared facility. Foreign Person Indoctrination Foreign persons employed by or assigned to NSI shall receive a briefing that addresses the following requirements: NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 57 of 74 www.NSIteam .com 1. Prior to the release of any ITAR protected unclassified information to them, an export authorization issued by ODTC needs to be obtained by NSI . 2. They are required to adhere to all of NSI’s security rules, policies, and procedures and employee personnel regulations that outline the specific information that has been authorized for release to them . 3. They are not permitted, under any circumstance, to have access to classified information without 1) being granted a special security clearance (highly unlikely occurrence for foreign n ationals) and 2) having an export license in effect for the subject transaction. Additionally, if access to classified information is ever granted, they must agree to send and receive all such data via NSI's security office. 4. All technical work -related info rmation received by them and technical work- related information that they need to forward from NSI shall be prepared in English . 5. They may not attempt to gain access to any data/information, either electronic or physical, or storage containers that have exp ort control or security classification markings, or elec tronic files that are password or otherwise protected . 6. They will be subject to sanctions that, depending upon circumstances, may include loss of job, should they willfully, or by negligence or gross d isregard, violate any of NSI's security/export policies and procedures . Lump -sum cash awards will be granted in recognition of a task “above and beyond” expectations that results in either tangible or intangible enhancement of NSI’s support to i ts customers or improvements in corporate practices. The qualifications and disbursement of the award will be based on the guidelines listed below. The majority of awards will be in the amount of $250. Only in exceptional circumstances and with accompanyi ng justification by the award nominator will larger amounts not to exceed $500 be considered by the Award Committee. SSCCOOPPEE 1. Provide NSI e mployees a definition of the SPOT policy. 2. Outline eligibility requirements, criter ia and procedures for the SPOT program. 3. Outline award payouts for the SPOT program. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy is outlined below . GGEENNEERRAALL All NSI employees are eligible to receive awards at any time under the SPOT program with the exception of: 1. Consultants, sub- contractors, co nsulting employees, members of advisory boards and NSI employees working less than half- time; 2. Executives of NSI (e.g., CEO, President, Chief Scientists and VPs); 3. An employee who has been employed with NSI for less than 90 days ; 4. An employee who has received an NSI SPOT in the previous 60 days . In order for an employee to become eligible he/she should have demonstrated superior performance in at least one of the following areas: 1. An identifiable and exceptional contribution (i.e., well beyond what is expecte d of an employee of similar rank or that fall within an employee’s job specification) to NSI’s business development and /or financial goals ; 2. An identifiable and exceptional scientific, technical and/or analytical contribution to one or more of NSI’s contrac ted projects; 3. A significant improvement in or contribution to NSI corporate processes and procedures ; 4. Development of a proven and marketable new capability or software tool . SSPPAA AAWWAARRDD PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE Candidate awardees must be nominated in writing by either a) the employee’s supervisor, or b) the PI or PM on a project or non -billable work (e.g., bid and proposal) which the cand idate has supported for 40 hours or more. Nominations for awards can be submitted at any time, but shou ld be submitted to the SPOT Commi ttee Chair on the NSI SPOT Nomination form and signed by the nominator. Multiple eligible nominators may sign the same nomination form. In those instances when the qualification of the award is not clear, the Committee may request additional information fr om the nominator. NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 62 of 74 www.NSIteam .com The Chair will call a meeting (either via telecon ference or email) of the SPOT Committee within 7 da ys of receipt of an award nomination. The Committee will have up to 7 days to deliberate and review the nomination and decide whether to grant the proposed award. In some instances, the Committee will request additional information from the nominator. As a general rule, the total time from receipt of nomination to Committee decision should not exceed 14 calendar days, but in some instances it may take longer in the event additional information is required. In no case should a decision not be rendered within 30 calendar days. Once a decisi on is made, the Chair of the SPOT Committee will notify in writing the nominator, the direct supervisor (if different), the CEO and Director of Finance & Admin of the decision. In the case where an award will be made, the Committee Chair will coordinate the completion of the award process with the CEO and Director of Finance & Admin. The Nominator will info rm the candidate of the Committee’s decision and award amount (if applicable). If an award nominee in good standing gi ves notification of intent to resign or retire between the time he/she was nominated and the award presentation, he/she is still eligible for the award. In the event of death of the nominee, any award granted will be paid to the estate beneficiary. The SPOT program and payment of all cash rewards is contingent upon the availability of sufficient funds within the company for the purpose of this program. NSI reserves the right to change or terminate the SPOT program at any time . Inappropriate and/or inadvertent disclosur e of NSI’s trade secrets, proprietary information and/or inventions cou ld cause significant damage to NSI’s ability to compete in its various markets . PPOOLLIICCYY This Non -Disclosure and Inventions Agreement (the “Agreement”) sets forth and confirms the understanding between NSI (the “Company”) and the undersigned employee (“I” o r “me”) concerning certain of the terms and conditions under which the Company has agreed to utilize my services and I have agreed to be employed by the Company. In consideration of my hiring or my continued employment, whichever is applicable, by the Comp any and the compensation paid or to be paid to me, I agree as follo ws: 1. Non-Compete: a. The Employee undertakes, during the period of employment and for a period of 2 year(s) after the employment’s termination, not to, either directly or indirectly, conduct or in other manner further activitie s which directly competes with the Company’s business activ ities. b. Upon termination of the employment, the Employee shall not be entitled to take the Company's customers or former customers over to a company which competes with th e Company, including the Employee’s sole proprietorship. The Employee undertakes to relinquish these customers or for mer customers and shall, instead, endeavour to ensure that they remain with, or return to, the Company. The Employee's undertaking shall ap ply during the term of the employmen t and for a period of 2 years from the date of termination of the employment. c. "The Company's customers" shall mean those customers which the Company had at the time of the termination of the employment or has had during a period of 1 year prior thereto. "Customers" shall also mean potential customers who, at the time of termination of the employment or during a period of one (1) year prior thereto, conducted negotiations with the Company. 2. Non-Solicitation: The Employee u ndertakes to refrain, personally or through another party, from attempting to induce, or persuading Employees (and consultants) of the Company, to terminate their employment (or assignment) with the Company. The Employee’s undertaking shall a pply during the term of the employment and for a p eriod of 2 years from the date of termination of the employment. In addition hereto, such Employee or consultant may not be offered employment or assignment with any enterprise controlled by the Employee. 3. Company's Proprietary Information : I understand that in performance of my job duties with the Company, I will be exposed to the Company's Proprietary Information. “ Proprietary Information ” means information or material that is commercially valuable to the Company and no t generally known in the industry. This includes, but is not limited to: a. any and all versions of the Company's proprietary computer software, hardware, firmware and documentation; b. technical information concerning the Company's products a nd services, including product data and specifications, know -how, formulae, diagrams, flow charts, drawings, source code, object code, program listings, test results, processes, inventions, research projects and product development; c. information concerning the Company's business, including cost information, pro fits, sales information, accounting and unpublished financial information, business plans, and marketing methods, customer lists and customer information, purchasing techniques, supplier lists and supplier information an d advertising strategies; NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 72 of 74 www.NSIteam .com d. informatio n concerning the Company's employee salaries; e. information submitted by the Company's customers, suppliers, employees, consultants or co - ventures with the Company for study, evaluation or use; and f. any o ther information no t generally known to the public whic h, if misused or disclosed, could reasonably be expected to adversely affect the Company's business. 4. Nondisclosure of Proprietary Information : I will keep the Company's Proprietary Information, whethe r or not prepared o r developed by me, in the strictest confidence. I will not use or disclose such secrets to others without the Company's written consent, except when necessary to perform my job. However, I shall have no obligation to treat as confidentia l any information w hich: a. was in my possession or known to me, without an obligation to keep it confidential, before such information was disclosed to me by the Company; b. is or becomes public knowledge through a source other than me and through no fault of m ine; or c. is or becom es lawfully available to me from a s ource other than the Company. 5. Confidential Information of Others : I will not disclose to the Company, use in the Company's business, or cause the Company to use, any information or material that is a trade secret of oth ers. 6. Return of Materials: When my e mployment with the Company ends, for whatever reason, I will promptly deliver to the Company all originals and copies of all documents, records, software programs, media and other materials containing any of the Company' s Proprietary Information. I will al so return to the Company all equipment, files, software programs and other personal property belonging to the Company. 7. Confidentiality Obligation Survives Employment : I understand that my obligation t o maintain the confidentiality and security of the Comp any's Proprietary Information remains with me even after my employment with the Company ends and continues for so long as such material remains a trade secret. 8. Inventions a. I agree to disclose promptly, completely and in writing to the Company any work of a uthorship, discovery, process, design, innovation, development, improvement or invention, whether or not patentable and whether reduced to practice or not, which I discover, conceive and/or develop, either individually o r jointly with others (whether on or off the Company’s premises or during or after working hours) during the term, and within the scope, of my employment with the Company, and which was or is related to the business (e.g., current contra cts, products, past work) or proposed business (e.g., p roposals, white papers, business plans) of the Company. In the event the Company is unable, after reasonable effort, to secure my signature on any document or instrument necessary to secure trademarks, letters patent, co pyrights or other analogous protecti on relating to an Invention, I hereby irrevocably designate and appoints the Company and its duly authorized officers and agents as my agent and attorney -in-fact, to act for an on my behalf and stead t o execute and file any applications and to do all other lawfully permitted acts to further the prosecution and issuance of trademarks, letters patent, copyright or other analogous protection thereon with the same legal force and effect as if executed by me. b. I hereby assign a nd agree to assign to the Company wi thout any separate or additional remuneration my entire right, title and interest in all such Inventions, together with any and all United States and foreign rights thereto. I understand that all Inven tions, which I do h ereby assign and agree to assign, ar e and shall become the exclusive property of the Company, whether or not patent applications are filed therefore, and I agree to treat such Inventions as Proprietary Information. c. Modification: This Agreement may not be modified except by a writing signed both by the Company and me. f. Assignment: This Agreement may be assigned by the Company. I may not assign or delegate my duties under Agreement without Company's prior written approval. --- Extracted from: 3.10_Overtime_Policy_and_Extended_Hours.pdf ---

NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 49 of 74 www.NSIteam .com PPOOLLIICCYY NNOO.. 001166:: PPAAIIDD OOVVEERRTTIIMMEE AANNDD EEXXTTEENNDDEEDD HHOOUURRSS PPUURRPPOOSSEE The purpose of this policy is to document the policy for the conditions under which pai d overtime and extended hours will be authorized and how it will be managed by NSI. SSCCOOPPEE NSI paid overtime and extended hours policy. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE The procedure for this policy is outlined below . GGEENNEERRAALL PPOOLLIICCYY AANNDD PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE All employees will be paid onc e per month on the last work day of the month. For paydays falling on a Saturday or holiday, you will be paid the prior business day. For paydays falling on a Sunday, you will be paid the following business day. NSI highly encourages all employees to use d irect deposit of their checks. If you are absent on payday and someone else is to pick up your check, it will not be released without a s igned, handwritten note from you authorizing the named person to pick it up. The person designated to pick up your check will be asked to produce identification satisfactory to management; otherwise, your check will not be released. Any deviations from thi s procedure must have prior approval from the NSI CE O. It is NSI's standard policy to expect all professional (exempt) employees to complete their assignments working no more than 40 hours per week. Notwithstanding, NSI recognizes that occasional situatio ns arise that require professional staff to work extended hours (more than 40 hours per week). Paid overtime (exceeding 40 hours per week) for salaried employees, at a straight hourly rate, will be used only in the event of special staffing requirements th at cannot be satisfied by any other reasonable means. Such additional pay, where approved by the employee supervisor an d NSI C EO, will be at an amount equivalent to 1/40th of the employee’s regular weekly salary for each extra hour worked. Vacation, sick/personal and holiday pay will be paid on the regular pay cycle. If you resign, final settlement of services or wages wi ll be made no earlier than the next regular pay cycle, or in accordance with state law, whichever is sooner. If you are terminated, you w ill be issued a check on the next regular payday, or in accordance with applicable state law, whichever is earlier. Payout of vacation will be limited to 160 hours. There will be no payout for sick/personal leave. AAPPPPLLIICCAABBIILLIITTYY This po licy applies to all employees; however an individual's treatment under this policy is dependent upon their employment status (exempt vs. n on-exempt). Exempt employees are typically salaried or part -time hourly professionals that have a large degree of freedom in deciding how to accomplish their work tasks. They are referred to as 'exempt' because certain labor laws, that guarantee such thing s as overt ime pay, do not apply to them. Non -exempt personnel are typically employees that work on an hourly basis in non - professional po sitions where they exercise a limited amount of discretion. PPRROOCCEEDDUURREE It should be recognized that overtime and additi onal work other than that which is regularly scheduled might be required. Overtime will be paid to eligible, non -exempt employees in acco rdance with applicable state law. The pay for regular overtime will be at the federal or state prescribed wage rate, wh ichever is higher. All overtime must be authorized prior to its occurrence by your immediate supervisor and the NSI CE O. All overtime wi ll be clearly noted on your time sheet and should be initialed by your immediate supervisor. Managers that supervise no n-exempt employees may authorize overtime to the extent that the associated NSI, Inc. Policies and Procedures Page 50 of 74 www.NSIteam .com costs do not exceed their budget. Overtime must be authorized in advance by the NSI C EO and the authorizing manager who is then responsible for ensuring that the overtime is utiliz ed efficiently and effectively. Non-Exempt Employee Overtime Managers that supervise non- exempt employees may authorize overtime to the extent that the associated costs do not exceed their budget. Overtime must be authorized in advance and the authorizing manager is responsible for ensuring that the overtime is utilized efficiently and effectively. NSI will pay pre -authorized overtime to non -exempt hourly employees at the rate of 150% for all time worked in excess of 40 hours in a one week pay period. Exempt Employee Overtime The NSI CE O will consider authorizing extended hours (extra pay for exempt personnel) under the following circumst ances: − There are pending staffing requirements that cannot be effectively met by: o moving personnel between assignments ; o requesting contract extensions; or o the use of contract personnel. − The staffing dilemma cannot be resolved by staff increases either bec ause: o the need is too short -term in nature to make hiring a prudent decision, or o the required talent is not readily ava ilable in the labor market. The NSI CE O will review the work backlog on all ongoing contracts and determine which jobs, if any, should be candidates for extended hours. If a decision is made to evoke extended hours under any contract, employees will be in formed in writing by an “Extended Hours Notice” that specifies the anticipated period of extended hours and the contracts affected. This notice, by itself, does not authorize additional pay, but rather, informs employees that NSI is in extended hour’s mode on specific contracts. Additional pay for extra hours worked by an exempt employee must also be verbally authorized by the Project Mana ger prior to being worked. After the Extended Hours Notice is given, the Project Manager should coordinate additional h ours worked with individual project personnel. The following items should be mutually agreed to during the authorization discussion betwe en the Project Manager and the employee: − The number of hours the employee is expected to work during the extended hour s period (or shorter period, such as the next week, if more appropriate). − The technical objectives the employee will direct his efforts t owards during such additional hours. − A general agreement on the time (i.e. week- ends, nights) and place (i.e. home, off ice) where the additional hours will be worked. − If an employee feels that additional time is needed to accomplish certain technical objec tives, he must secure the Project Manager's verbal approval prior to expending the additional time. All professional ( exempt) staff working extended hours will be paid at a rate equivalent to 1/40th of their weekly salary for the number of hours worked in excess of the calendar month's normal billable hours (calculated by multiplying the number of week days in the calenda r month by 8).

Our focus has been to deliver innovative social science solutions to government clients for a variety of national security and operational imper atives. Our government clients want insights and a rich understanding of the overwhelming complexity of people and their behaviors for various critically important and co mplex decision -making problems. In 2011, expanding and diversifying our client base was a top priority. Our strategy was to provide our analytic expertise to clients in the commercial sector needing to better understand customers and their behaviors. We focused on bringing greater discipline to measuring customer interactions, sentiment, and service. We successfully piloted a project with a major video game developer then and since have substantially grown this wor k. Our Vision : Enable clients to make more informed and better decisions on complex decision -making problems through our multidisciplinary data -driven analytics. Our Mission: Create value for our clients by improving their decision -making processes questioning assumptions, thinking deeply, and generating clarifying insights. To learn more about our organization, its history, and how we can help organizations such as yours to get the most out of you r data, make better decisions, and maximize your success, watch: NSI Promotional Video To download an overview brochure of NSI, click: NSI Overview Brochure Diverse Multidisciplinary Team Multiple Analytic Methods NSI is highly diverse and multidisciplinary. Our researchers and analysts have expertise in social psychology, statistics, research methods, economics, cultural anthropology, decision science, business management, predictive modeling, political science, international relations, communications, mathematics, computer science, and other disciplines. Understanding people and their behaviors is inherently complex, ambiguous, and riddled with uncertainty. It is also not amenable to rigid analytical approaches based on a single methodology. NSI has significant expertise and many years of hands-on experien ce applying quantitative, qualitative, and mixed- method research and analytic methods. Nationally Recognized Leaders Domain | Industry Experience NSI’s leadership is comprised of nationally recognized experts with diverse backgrounds from premier government, industry, and academic institutions. They include current and former professors from top universities, former senior Defense Department and industry executives, and members/co -chairs of National Academy of Sciences studies. NSI has been supporting government clients for years in numerous problem domains spanning security, stability, deterrence, reconstruction, violent extremism, radicalization, and counterterrorism. In our commercial work we support clients from the gaming, d igital entertainment, business intelligence, and customer service sectors. Likewise, education exceeding the minimum shown may be substituted for experience. Degree Substituted Experience Associates Can be substituted for a High School Diploma and 2 additional years’ relevant experience Bachelors Can be substituted for an Associates Degree and 2 additional years’ relevant experience; or a High School Diploma and 4 additional years’ relevant experience Masters Can be substituted for a Bachelors Degree and 2 additional years’ relevant experience; or an Associates Degree and 4 additional years’ relevant experience; or a High School Diploma and 6 additional years’ relevant experience PhD Can be substituted for a Masters Degree and 2 additional years’ relevant experience; or a Bachelors Degree and 4 additional years’ relevant experience; or a High School Diploma and 8 additional years’ relevant experience
